Subject: Re: Thundr

I think the hate stirred up by a few people on this system
for each other is really terrible.  Instead of saying things
like 'Thunder is stupid!' or 'Kill Roscoe' or 'You are all
liers!" or whatever, why not just simply state opinion/possible
fact, instead of maliciously gossiping to each other to try and
destroy everyone else?
An example of this is the message supposedly left by Susan Thunder
saying she was back.  That is an obvious fake.  Any fool can
see the "'" after the name.  That changes the entire account name,
so that it may LOOK like it was from thunder, but it wasn't.  These
cheap shots and tricks are really making me feel sick.  How about
some civility and humility, instead of jeering, taunting anger?
                               -Tim Bessie (sysop on Onyx)

Message number 6958 is 20 lines from Cheshire Catalyst
To all at 11:30:25 on 06-Mar-81.
Subject: The Controversy

While Ms Thunder may not be the most respectable of phreaks and
hackers (and I do fault her for not showing the "True Hacker"
ideals), any user can log into this system, if you haven't noticed,
and pull off enough info to start tracking down phreaks. A certain
level of paranoia is healthy in this businexxxx hobby. While it certainly
could be Susan who's turning any one in, see what kind of trail you may
be leaving yourself. Also, the term True Hacker is one that may need
some interpreting. It means someone who is friendly to systems that
are friendly. BBS's in general are friendly, and should be helped by
all. They should not be crashed, phones turned off, power cut, or
other nastyness, because then they won't be there to play with
anymore. The hobbyists attitude should certainly be one of "Sure, 
I can crash it". In certain cases, there may even be reason to crash it,
but to say "I won't crash it" shows more responsibility than than
the child-like hackers can come up with. When you know you have the power
to be nasty, it doesn't mean that you have to use it. Especially when
you can hurt people in the process. Computer hobbyists have shown an
increasing tendency towards anarchy. Being a staffer on TAP, I can't 
claim not to hold some of these ideas. But look through some of the
liturature. Most of the good stuff is fiction. (continued)


Message number 6959 is 18 lines from Cheshire Catalyst
To all at 11:37:11 on 06-Mar-81.
Subject: The Controversy (continued)

I would like to refer you to Ayn Rand (The Fountainhead, Atlas
Shrugged), but more fun to read are the books of Robert A Heinlein
(Stranger in a Strange Land, Space Cadet, Red Planet, >The Moon
Is A Harsh Mistress<). The last, is a great computer story. It shows a
computer "Coming Alive" as more circuits are hooked up, and how it
learns about jokes. What is always-funny, and what is funny-once, ect.
The ability to crash systems, and make life hard for others is not
one that should be used for those purposes. If you can crash a system, 
you can help that system be useful to others who don't know systems
as well as you. Sharing that knowledge can be frustrating, but the more
people start to learn about computers, the more computers there will be
around for us to play with. Have fun, folks, I know that I sure do,
but keep it cool. 
 
   Keep Smiling,
     Cheshire
 
PS: and keep others smiling too.

Subject: "susan 'thunder"

It is obivious that the person leaving messages as "Susan 'Thunder"
is a fake. Here are the reasons:
1) This person is using an Apple as a terminal. The real Susan
   Thunder uses a regular 80 col terminal.
2) The messages from "Ms. 'Thunder" are all in UPPERCASE.
   More evidence of an apple.
3) This person is signing "her" messages as
               "THUNDR@AI MIT"
   which, for those who aren't aware of it, is the WRONG SYNTAX for
   an Arpanet mailing address at MIT.
4) As Tim Bessie pointed out, this system will not accept a signon
   for "Susan Thunder" without the proper password, so to bypass
   this, this person is signing in as "Susan 'Thunder" to beat this.
 
I'm certain that others could find errors in phrasing, etc that Susan would
not do, as well as claiming knowledge she wouldn't have. 
       So, now let's ask ourselves this: Who hates Susan so much that
this person would totally screw up her hacking existance by making her
totally disreputable?

Message number 6978 is 17 lines from Peter Alfke
To Phil Reed at 20:23:27 on 06-Mar-81.
Subject: Nucleons

You are correct, nucleons are general subatomic particles, and so
were the nucleons that I was talking about in my message. Perhaps
(actually probably) I did not mention this: the 'nucleons' that I was
referring to are any subatomic particle, WITH 'k spin' which is a
complex spin extending through a 7-dimensional hyperspace. Application
of this spin changes the properties of particles in unusual (to say the
least!) ways, and by 'nucleons' I meant 'nucleons under k spin'.
I should have been more clear there. Thanks for catching that. Look up
the article if you really want to know the whole story; it's quite
interesting.
(Application of k spin is the most difficult part, with spin in each
successive dimension much more difficult than the last. Eight-dimensional
spin has been considered and could possibly be achieved with very very
strange techniques, but it would extend the range of the nucleonic
powers to such a degree (several light-years) that creation of one
such nucleon would destroy everything in the universe... Ick.
                                    --Pete

Message number 7004 is 9 lines from SYSOP
To Rick Mainhart at 19:08:10 on 07-Mar-81.
Subject: Noisy line

Hi Rick,
   What you were experiencing could be due to a bad line.  It might
also have been caused by someone trying to do a 'emergency verify'
on this line.  The 'emergency verify' was a trick some people used
to try and dump the current user so they could get on.  It opens
the line for a few hundred millisec's.  8BBS doesn't drop the line
unless carrier has been lost for over a second.  So the 'emergency
verify' can cause garbage char's, but at least you stay connected.
  Regards,..

Message number 7019 is 19 lines from SYSOP
To John Limpert at 10:21:26 on 08-Mar-81.
Subject: DES things

Hi John,
   Nice to see someone else interested in 'secure communication'.  From
what I've read, it seems that the NBS DES encryption method is secure
from exhaustive key search attacks for at least the next 8-10 years.
The alledged reason the NSA asked IBM to classify some of their working
papers on the DES algorithm was that IBM accidently (independantly)
duplicated some of the methods that NSA uses to crack foreign gov't
traffic.  There was a back issue of BYTE mag that had a good description
of the DES algorithm.  The NBS will only certify hardware implementations
of the algorithm 'cause they say that a software emulation could be
compromised.  I've got spec sheets for the INTEL, WD, and AMD chips.
I plan to use the WD (Western Digital) chip because it is fast, easy to
interface and simple to program.  It is available locally for about $70.
Any of the DES chips would be compatible with each other at the message
level.  One of the major drawbacks to the use of the DES for BBS msg's
is that it requires some secure way of exchanging the keys.  I'm trying
to get some info on the Hellman and Diffie 'public key' system.  It
sounds like it would be much better suited for BBS use.  Let me know
if you have any ideas for applying DES or other methods to BBS msg's.

Message number 7071 is 20 lines from Meg Kazmar
To mark mosko at 20:52:39 on 09-Mar-81.
Subject: books

mark,
  here are some good books on compilers...arranged in order
from most practical to most abstract:
1.  The Anatomy of a Compiler, John Lee, Van Nostrand Reinhold,
        1967. (describes the implementation of a FORTRAN compiler)
2.  Compiler Construction for Digital Computers, David Gries,
        John Wiley & Sons, 1971.
3.  Principles of Compiler Design, Aho & Ullman, Addison-Wesley,
        1978.
4.  Compiler Design Theory, Lewis, Rosenkrantz, & Sterns, Addison-
        Wesley, 1976.
5.  Theory of Parsing, Translation & Compiling, Vol. I: Parsing,
        Vol. II: Compiling, Aho & Ullman, Prentice-Hall, 1972.
          (very abstract)
**Collections of papers on compiler implementation:
1.  Programming Systems and Languages, Editor - Saul Rosen,
        McGraw-Hill, 1967.  (Part 3: Compiling & Translating)
2.  Compiler Techniques, Editor - B. Pollack, Auerbach, 1972.
3.  Compiler Construction: An Advanced Course, Editors -
        Bauer & Eickel, Springer-Verlag, 1976.


Message number 7072 is 17 lines from Meg Kazmar
To mark mosko at 21:10:30 on 09-Mar-81.
Subject: more books

as far as languages go, Professor White at Stevens Institute of
Technology, Hoboken, N.J. had written a set of notes used for
teaching MACRO-10 around 1973.  They may still be available from
the Stevens book store.  Two other references on MACRO-10:
1.  DECSYSTEM-10/DECSYSTEM-20 Hardware Reference Manual.
2.  DECSYSTEM-10 Assembly Lanuage Manual.
      (both available from DEC)
      (if you want the order numbers, let me know...)
For MACRO-11 the PDP-11 Assembly Language Manual and any of the
11 Series Processor Handbooks will describe the instruction set.
These, too, available from DEC.
------
For LISP:
 try:  LISP 1.5 Primer, Clark Weissman, Dickenson, 1967.
 
Hope this is helpful...   have fun!
            /meg

Message number 7088 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To Bill Murray at 06:21:48 on 10-Mar-81.
Subject: Call Waiting and Modems

The best way to prevent Call Waiting from disturbing your data
connection is to temporarily disable it.  Call Waiting is "off"
under the following circumstances:
 
       1. If you forward you calls somewhere.
       2. From the time you begin to make a three-way
          call until you have connected everyone together
          and the third party has gone off-hook (answered).
 
In a Number 2 ESS there are some additional conditions under
which Call Waiting is disabled, such as while you are waiting
for a long distance call to answer, and for the entire duration
of a three-way call.
 
I strongly recommend using Call Forwarding, since it doesn't tie up
any of Mother's precious resources.  The only problems are figuring
out something reasonable to forward to (preferably something that is
always busy (watch out, some of Bell's busy test #s "answer")) and
remembering to cancel it when you are done.  The other method is to
call some recording and then add-on 8bbs without connecting both.

INTEL  8294 Data Encryption Unit   (80 bytes/sec)

NBS as valid implementations of the DES algorithm.  Regards,..


Message number 7125 is 18 lines from SYSOP
To Synthesized speech experimente at 09:25:48 on 11-Mar-81.
Subject: VOTRAX  SC-01 group buy

A recent issue of BYTE magazine contained an article on VOTRAX
speech synthesizer work.  VOTRAX now sells a single chip phoneme
synthesizer that is capable of generating continous, high quality
speech, of unlimited vocabulary, from low data rate inputs.
  The SC-01 chip contains 64 different phonemes that are addressed
by a 6 bit code.  The inflection (pitch level) of the voiced
phonemes can be varied with a 2 bit code.  The SC-01 is very easy
to interface to a 8 bit parallel I/O port.  All that is needed is
is the 8 data bits (6 +2), an output strobe pulse.  The only
input from the SC-01 is a 'busy' line that indicates when it is
ready to accept a new phoneme.  The output from the SC-01 is the
audio speech signal which is amplified to drive a speaker.
  Now the hard part.  VOTRAX will only sell a minimum quantity of
5 chips at $95. each.  I already know a couple of people that want
one.  What is needed are a few more people who would like to get
this chip.  I'll co-ordinate the buy when we get 5 firm commitments
from people for $95.  Leave a msg if you want to get the chip for
$95.  If you want spec sheets, call VOTRAX at 313 588-0341.  Regards,..

Message number 7184 is 13 lines from John Wood
To bernard klatt at 01:44:52 on 13-Mar-81.
Subject: wd chip set

HI again, gee, i would proceed very carefully with ordering that
chip set.  All the micro-computer experience i have with Western
Digital indicates they *love* to have their customers debug their
lsi hardware for them.
For example, the wd1771 disc controller worked fine, but the 1791
had a bug that often resulted in the inability to read a disc 
written with the 1771.  Also, the infamous 'micro-engine' which is
their pdp-11 (lsi-11) re-coded to execute p-code had so many bugs
in it they actually are swapping the entire chip set to all users
for free (but so far, one guy I know has been waiting to get his
micro-engine cpu board BACK from WD for 4 months!!!!)
PRoceed with caution, even if the chip is certified, they might
have  hand-picked a good one when they submitted it!!!!

Message number 7195 is 14 lines from Ed Smith
To sysop at 06:52:59 on 13-Mar-81.
Subject: Timing for carrier tone

Hi! Can you change the parameter which controls the timing on
your carrier tone generation upon initial dail-in? I lost
the connection and had to re-dial several tiimes, which
is oppressive when doing it long distance, because your
machine only gives the tone for 7 seconds (I timed it instead
of trying once). Long carrier detect delay, which is the standard
on many devices, can take from 2.5 up to 6 seconds; if it doesn't
have all that time, it may not repsond and let your line
drop even with a good connection. When you cound the time needed
to react to hearing the tone and putting the receiver in the
acoustic coupler, that subtracted from 7 seconds doesn't leave
enough time. Please double your time to at least 15 seconds.
It shouldn't cost you anything, and would save your callers
trouble. Thanks

Message number 7199 is 14 lines from SYSOP
To Ed Smith at 11:45:03 on 13-Mar-81.
Subject: Carrier detect time-out

Hi Ed,
    Yes, I've noticed that some callers are a bit sluggish
about getting things together when calling 8BBS.  The
modem is currently set to disconnect after 6 sec's if no
carrier is present.  The other setting is an 18 sec time-
out.  The problem with the 18 sec timeout is that (for
local callers)  the line is still busy when they re-dial
the number.   I really can't understand why it should take
more than about 2-3 sec's after 8BBS modem answers to 
have your equipment send a carrier.  If you don't get a 
busy signal - you know 8BBS modem will answer.  However,..
I will temporarily change the switch to allow 18 sec time-
out.  If there are any complaints about the 18 sec setting
it will go back to 6 sec.  Regards,..

Subject: Re: Onyx availability

********************     ONYX    **********************
Everyone:  The Onyx is NOT (repeat NOT) down.  The
'ferns' account does not work at the moment, though.  This
is because the present version of the C compiler we have
often messes up when it comes to character-arrays, and thus
messes up file accounting and buffering.  We are presently
polling for a new version of both the operating system AND
the compiler.  When this is done, the 'ferns' account at
(408) 425-8000
will be graciously revived.  Also, I am changing the message
system to work through a system of protections.  Thus, people I
trust more will be able to access various things accordingly.
The only thing that really needs to be guarded is the 'system'
command, by which one may enter the Onyx Unix Version 7 Operating
System itself.  The only problem with this is that people might
decide they want to go and delete the message and accounting
files for ferns.  Everything else is safe.  So, if you want to
use the main OS, and I don't trust you, or 'ferns' is down, then
you may log in as account 'guest' (lower case), no password.
That is ABSOLUTELY FREE, and you get ALL PRIVILEDGES of a normal

Message number 7234 is 15 lines from Tim Bessie
To Marc Mosko at 23:20:08 on 13-Mar-81.
Subject: Re: Compiler book

One of the best compiler books I have read (as an introduction
to compiler-writing) is:
An Introduction to Compiler Writing
   By J. S. Rohl (MacDonald and Jane's/American Elsevier
                  Computer Monographs, 1975)
This book describes the construction of a compiler, starting with
a very small, restricted subset of Algol, and expanding it until
it has described a full Algol compiler, with info methods,
optimization, etc.  It doesn't delve too deeply (at all)
into theory, which is what I liked about it.  Once you have
read it, you will be ready to write your own compiler quite
quickly.  Also, it does not discuss much of the rhetorical
questions about compilers over and over, so it is only about
300 fast-reading pages long.  Look into it.
                                       -Tim Bessie

Message number 7285 is 8 lines from SYSOP
To Richard Diaz at 21:03:55 on 14-Mar-81.
Subject: Disco & J. Hubbard

Hi Richard,
   The disconnect could be due to 101 things that go wrong at this end,
your end, telco stuff in-between, etc...
   When you enter a RP msg, 8BBS verifies that the 'WHO TO:' name is
in the user name file.  If you spell it wrong, it won't accept a RP
msg.  You can use the  I  function to find a user name, or do a  S
summary and find a msg from that person if you don't remember the
spelling.  Regards,..

Message number 7298 is 6 lines from SYSOP
To Eric Moyer at 12:35:07 on 15-Mar-81.
Subject: MK5087 cont'd

Hi Eric,
   Next time you buy an 'exotic' part, you really should get the data
sheet.  I can't imagine why the BYTE article shows the xtal hooked to
+12 since the data sheet clearly shows that the xtal is connected
only to pins 7 & 8.  There are no other components and no other
connections.  Give it a try.  Regards,..


Message number 7299 is 14 lines from SYSOP
To All at 12:45:08 on 15-Mar-81.
Subject: 8BBS - 1 year old

    8BBS has now been on-line for one full year.  It has survived...
- several earthquakes
- power outages
- system crashers
- death threats to the SYSOP
- PT&T monitoring
- phone phreak pranking
and 48 revisions to the software.
   There have been no hardware failures in the system (DEC makes good
equipment), but the Novation modem has had a few problems.  Perhaps it
wasn't meant for 12,000 + calls.
   There are no plans for multi-user operation, but there will at least
one or two more revisions to the software.  8BBS may even get a 1200
baud modem sometime later this year.   Regards,..


Message number 7300 is 15 lines from SYSOP
To Chuck George at 13:02:11 on 15-Mar-81.
Subject: Problems

Hi Chuck,
   I noticed your comments about 8BBS.  I too would prefer not to see
personal attacks and foul language on 8BBS, but since it is a 'public
access' system, just about anyone can leave just about any kind of
msg.  I travel a lot and don't have time to sit an monitor what people
type into their msg's.  If you see a msg you dislike, attempt to kill
it, even if unsuccessful, it will show in the log file.  If there are
several people that object to a msg, it will probably disappear soon.
   Some users may not wish to be associated with a BBS that allowed
ads from your company, but if you wish to leave recruitment ads on
8BBS, that is fine with me.  You can 'kill protect' them, and of course
there is no charge.
   I did not understand what you meant by "... IF A PERSON HAS A LOT OF
TROUBLE WITH A COMPANY IT SHOULD BE KNOWN TO ALL AS WELL AS THE GOOD ONES."
   Regards,..

Message number 7318 is 9 lines from John Wood
To sysop at 04:26:02 on 16-Mar-81.
Subject: 1200 baud

Are you considering the vadic triple modem?  That is the
most versatile and allows virtually any kind of 1200 bauder
to call in. (IT supports Bell 212 and Vadic 3400, which are the two
universal 1200 baud protocols , which , of course, are not compatible
with each other. (Like Telenet has two sets of lines for 1200, one
are vadic and the other are Bell.  A real pain if you forget which
one is which unless you have your own triple modem.)
The price $900 is a little too steep, otherwise cbbs santa clara
would have had one a long time ago.

Message number 7393 is 15 lines from Eric Moyer
To SYSOP at 19:38:08 on 17-Mar-81.
Subject: Auto-dialer

I found out where an autodialer can be connected to a
phone where it will be blocked from getting ringer and
dialing voltages. Connect it to the same terminals on the
terminal block inside a standard phone as the voice
transmitter in the handpiece. If you have a direct-connect
modem connected to the line, then connect the dialer AFTER
the isolation x-former in the modem; I found out that even
a 2500 ohm load will load down the phone line too much
and prevent the phone or modem from hanging up! Also, put
another isolation/load matching x-former between the modem/phone
and the autodialer to block ringer voltages. The x-former
that I used is a T-31X made by Triad. It is rated for use
above 60Hz, and should block tthe 20Hz ringer voltage. I have
several of these x-formers if you would want one.Regards...
                                         Eric

Message number 7440 is 7 lines from SYSOP
To Kerry Abel at 00:27:30 on 19-Mar-81.
Subject: RP restrictions

Hi Kerry,
   The 'Read Protect' msg idea has always been a problem area.  8BBS doesn't
take any chances when working with RP msg's.  The next version of 8BBS will
allow you to Get and Kill RP msg's that are TO / FROM you if, (only if) you
have assigned yourself an access password with the U function.  If you don't
have a pw'd someone else could log in with your name and Get or Kill your
RP msg's, so that is why it now has those restrictions.  Regards,..

Message number 7446 is 20 lines from Tim Bessie
To ALL at 01:47:53 on 19-Mar-81.
Subject: Onyx accounts

In order to get an account, you must supply me with the following
information:
1) Your full, real name
2) The account NAME (NOT number) you want, which may be up to
       36 characters long, and is composed of any combonation
       of letters and/or numbers (no white spaces or odd chars)
3) The password you want, with the same restrictions as the
       account name.
Once I respond that your account has been initiated, call:
(408) 425-8000 for 300 baud and
(408) 425-8004 for 1200 baud (Ven-Tel 212A, I think)
and press return a couple of times.  When it says 'login: '
you type 'ferns' and press return.  If it asks you for
a password, then something has gone wrong.  It means either:
1) The account is missing for some strange reason
2) You are sending upper case and the login program doesn't
       convert to lower case
3) The characters you are sending have some bits set incorrectly
In any case, if something happens, leave me a message,  Try
several times.  Cont.


Message number 7447 is 15 lines from Tim Bessie
To ALL at 01:51:14 on 19-Mar-81.
Subject: Onyx, cont.

Once it has accepted the account name, it will (should) type
out the last login time, and, after a few seconds, say
"Account name: " (notice the difference between 'login: '
and 'Account name: ').  Once you have gotten this, type
in the account name I have assigned you, and press return.
If it doesn't know it, it will say so and log off, back to
the 'login: '.  If it does, it will greet you and ask for your
password with 'Enter Password: '.  Then enter the password I
have assigned you.  It should then log you in.  For your
first time, type 'help', 'menu', etc.  Commands cannot be
shortened, so, for instance, you may not use 'r' instead
of 'read'.  I am working on a way to make it possible to have
shortest-possible-alias type commands. In the meantime, ask me
for an account!
                               -Tim Bessie

Message number 7465 is 11 lines from SYSOP
To Bob Harrison at 08:57:28 on 19-Mar-81.
Subject: Bob Harrison

Hi Bob,
   No, the msg flagging code works fine.  I seem to recall someone using
your name that was attempting to login with oddball names, so I thought
6766 was appropriate.
   8BBS does not directly support multiple "WHO TO" msg's.  But you can
use the Get msg feature to copy msg's to several people.  I don't see
why you'd need to do that, since a public msg can be seen by everyone
and you can't Get RP msg's anyway.  If this is really important, let me
know, and I'll describe how it can be done.  The RP msg capability is
meant for private msg exchange between just two users, not pseudo-private
mail to a group of users.  Regards,..

Message number 7498 is 6 lines from SYSOP
To Allan Hessenflow at 17:57:32 on 20-Mar-81.
Subject: Prob's?

Hi Allan
   Not sure what happened to cause the 'hang' symptom.  If 8BBS stops
echoing the characters you type there are several things you can try
to get it going again.  Try a ^K, ^C, ^Q or S  to tell 8BBS to resume
output.  If a character that you typed got garbled, 8BBS might see it
as a S or ^S which would tell it to suspend output.  Regards,..

Message number 7521 is 9 lines from Richard Beal
To all at 09:03:30 on 21-Mar-81.
Subject: RADIO SCANNERS

Is anyone out there interested in exchanging radio frequencies for
the Santa Cruz-Monterey-Santa Clara California area?  I have a
Bearcat 250 scanner and over 100 confirmed frequencies on my list.
If you are interested in exchanging, obtaining a copy at cost or
just chatting about scanners please leave a message message here.
For the uninitiated, radio scanners use a microprocessor to quickly
scan and synthetically generate common radio frequencies.  The user
can easily listen into all kinds of public agencies (eg fire, police,
paramedics, car telephones, etc).  Great fun.

Message number 7537 is 20 lines from Susan Thunder
To Kerry Abel at 23:54:20 on 21-Mar-81.
Subject: Building Big-Macs

 
Hello.
 
I have alot of faith and respect for those dinky little game stamps that
fast food dives and supermarkets like to distribute.  Maybe it's just
because I've been extroidinarily lucky in the stupid games:  I don't
know...
The possibilty is very slim indeed that they have different "rare" game
pieces for different parts of the country, after all, it's just to easy
to "reach out, reach out and touch someone" if ya know what I mean.
There is also, however, another very slim possibility, and that is the
possibility that more than 2 or 3 million dollars worth of those prizes
will end up being claimed!  Most people get the thing, see if it's an
instant winner, and if not they trash it...most people figure that they
would never win anything.  Therefore, many of the rare pieces never make
it to collector's books, and it says in the rules that any prizes not
claimed will not be awarded.
Now to the luck I've had:  I found the "rare" piece to the $1,000 winner
in the last contest on the ground in the parking lot!!
cont.

Message number 7579 is 15 lines from Steven Inness
To ERIC MOYER at 01:28:49 on 23-Mar-81.
Subject: MK5087, etc

I assume you solved your MK5087 problem? what was
wrong? I didn't see your msg sooner, otherwise I 
could've helped you. From what I can tell, the misteak
is that pin 7 should NOT be wired to +12v and the
xtal should be wired from pin 7 to 8. the 5087 has
an internal resistor so the 1meg/10meg resistor should
not be needed. good luck. i might add that pin 7 is
internally wired to the input of an inverter and pin 8
is the output. this means you can use an external clock
wired to pin 7. you have probably solved your prob already.
i aggree, direct is MUCH better than using an xformer.
somewhere you have to isolate the computer from the line
though. i am somewhat perplexed about what the point
of adding the 2.5k resistor to the xformer was.
will talk later... -Dr. SLI, T.I.D.


Message number 7588 is 20 lines from Steven Inness
To sysop at 01:59:43 on 23-Mar-81.
Subject: datacom

regarding msg #6842 to bill murray about carrier loss:
call waiting, call forwarding, etc. I am 90% certain these
services are provided in your area. Read the front of 
your phone book. Certainly YOU should know at least what
legit services are avail. I feel your sys should tolerate
a 3 second carrier loss. Many commercial acoustic couplers
(my anderson jacobson for one) have a one second delay from
reception to xmission of carrier. this is so it will not be 
beeping when hearing speech, etc. They do not have this
delay at turn-off, the will stop xmitting within about
.1 sec. after loosing carrier. Let's say your mom lifts
up the downstairs phone and hearing the usual whine,
asks if you are on. Hearing no reply, she hangs up &
yells for you to get off the phone. (familiar, right?)
This incident resulted in a .25 sec hit (tech. name for
carrier loss (almost)) to the user's modem, which 
immediately drops carrier. .25 second later it recieves
carrier and starts its 1 sec countdown. Thus 1.25 secs
after the start of the dropout it turns on again only
to find our friendly 8bbs leaving... TBC...

Message number 7629 is 6 lines from SYSOP

Hi Larry,
   8BBS is mostly a "do it yourself" system.  If you want a password, just
help yourself by using the  U  function.  Some things you should know...
only the first 4 char's are used as the password.  When entering the
password you must also make sure the case matches (uppper case is NOT the
same as lower case).  Regards,..


Message number 7630 is 18 lines from SYSOP
To Robert Kohler at 09:03:10 on 24-Mar-81.
Subject: 8BBS secrets...

Hi Robert,
   As you can see from the I function, Dick hasn't been on for about a month.
So I'll try to answer the questions and let him know that you want to talk
to him.  The BASIC portion of 8BBS takes about 19K of 12bit words.  About 4K of
of that is stored ASCII prompt strings.  When a user is entering a msg, all
20 lines of 80 char's are stored in a string array and written to disk only
when the Save command is given.  The file structure is record I/O for all the
data files (User Name, User Data, Messages, Message Index) and sequential
I/O for all the text files (Other Systems, Help Info, Bulletins, Welcome).
Messages longer than 20 lines can be created by using a program to take a
OS/8 text file and insert it into the 8BBS message files.
   I'll be at the Faire on Friday, but I doubt if Dick plans to be there
any of the days.  I'll be passing out free 8BBS reference cards.  [NOTE:
to others... Don't bother to ask to me to mail you a card, get someone to
get it for you at the Faire].  About the clock 'accuracy',  that was a 
totally random coincidence that it was that close to NBS.  I re-enter the
time every evening after I restart the system.  It is often a minute or
two off since I don't enter the seconds.  Regards,..

Message number 7655 is 7 lines from Eric Moyer
To ALL / SYSOP at 07:37:10 on 25-Mar-81.
Subject: 8BBS Carrier

Note to everyone who has problems with 8BBS dropping carrier
before their modems can send carrier: Try holding down the
'0' on touch-tone systems--the tones generated fake out the
receiving modem into thinking that there is another modem,
so you can just hold down the '0' until your modem locks
onto the carrier, then let go. 
                                   Eric Moyer


Message number 7657 is 20 lines from Richard Beal
To SYSOP at 09:05:18 on 25-Mar-81.
Subject: Telenet prompts

From the TELENET users reference guide..."If you have any questions,
the Customer Service Desk (800-336-0437) will be happy to answer them."
 
TELENET signon procedure.  Dial access number.  Type 2 carriage returns.
When TELENET says "TERMINAL=" enter 4 character id for your terminal
or simply press return.  TELENET prompts with an @.  Type a C, skip
a space and typethe network address of the computer you want to talk to
followed by a carriage return.  It appears that the normal address format
is the telephone area code followed by a two digit number (e.g 408 45).
Other commands possible after the @ are D (disconnect from computer but
stay on TELENET), <cr>D<cr> to interrupt your computer session and return
to TELENET.  CONT<cr> to return to your computer session after being in
TELENET command mode.  FULL<cr> full duplex and HALF<cr> for no echo.
STAT<cr> gives id number of TELENET port you are using.  TAPE<cr> to
signify your input will be paper tape or cassette.
 
TELENET has a booklet (I don't know address) of various public Data Bases
that can be accessed via TELENET (provided of course you have an account
with that company).  


Message number 7661 is 8 lines from SYSOP
To Bruce Bennett at 12:30:20 on 25-Mar-81.
Subject: O list download

The Other systems list is just one file.  I can see no valid reason to
break it into several files.   8BBS does recognize the XON - XOF protocol.
This means that if your micro is loading data into a buffer it can send
XOF (^S) to 8BBS.  8BBS will then suspend transmission until your micro
is ready to receive more input.  Your micro then sends a XON (^Q) to 
tell 8BBS to resume transmission.  If you use this protocol, you should
be able to write the buffer to a disk file whenever you need to to avoid
losing info.  Regards,..

Message number 7693 is 11 lines from John Wood
To ALL IBM NOVICES at 02:15:29 on 27-Mar-81.
Subject: 3705 DATA-COM SYS

THE IBM 3705 IS AN ARCHAIC, OUTMODEM, BUT FULLY
FUNCTIONAL FRONT END DATA COMMUNICATIONS PROCESSOR
THAT IS USED ON ALL IBM GEAR FROM 360 UP TO 4331 AND
303X AS LINE CONTROLLERS AND NETWORK INTERFACES (UNLESS
YOU BUY A BETTER ONE FROM MEMOREX OR SOME THER PCM
VENDOR.)  IT IS OLD, BUT WORKS FINE.  IBM IS RUMOURED
TO BE READYING A REPLACEMENT FOR IT.
IT HANDLES CHARACTER LEVEL STUFF, MULTI-POINT POLLING,
ETC AND RELEIVES THE MAIN CPU AND I/O CHANNEL OF A LOT
OF THIS LOW-LEVEL, BUSY WORK.  IT MAY ALSO HAVE MULTIPLEXING
OR CONCENTRATING FUNCTIONS, BUT I AM NOT SURE ABOUT THAT.

OK, there is a nifty little box called a "V to U" converter that
takes all the cable channels including mid and super band and 
converts them to UHF. Its a broadband device so for example, the
"Z" channel on Theta cable in LA (pix carrier is 109.25 Mhz.) will
translate to UHF channel 45 with this device.  Some of the big
electronic stores in your aera should have them. Try Muntz if you
have one there, or else I can arrange to send you one.
This thing is totally legal, provided that the cable in your house
has the info, without having to tamper with any traps in the service
drop.  Some cable systems put "garbage" near the chroma carrier to 
foul up getting the movie channels, I have had no experience with
these systems.  Best bet for fooling around is over the air systems
(ON TV or Select) or Multipoint dist. systems, if youre into
microwave, or sat. TV if you got a big dish and LOW noise amp.
leave messages for me on PMS LA (213-291-9314), this thing is too

Message number 7768 is 8 lines from Phil Reed
To bill doger at 06:26:38 on 30-Mar-81.
Subject: thermal lances

Thermal lances have been around for several years. Putting one together
requires no great skill, just a basket full of money for the components.
Mosler and friends are busily trying to figure a way to block the
use of a lance, but all that heat has to end up somewhere! About the
only thing they've gotten is a safe with a refrigrated metal layer,
but even that's not good enough against the incredible amount of localized
heat.  I haven't seen the movie. I do hope they were wearing gas masks.
                                       ...phil

Message number 7770 is 15 lines from John Gilmore
To sysop at 07:40:18 on 30-Mar-81.
Subject: trapdoor ciphers

The big problem with these is that they are VERY expensive in terms
of computation.  Encoding a message with thexRivest/etc method
involves breaking it up into thepequivalent of 100-digit nubers
and then multiplying them by the key.  Know any fast 10x100
multiply routines?  Care to iterate over a long message with one?
 
It's also expensiveto find a key-pair (encoding/decoding keys).
It's of course not nearly as expensive as finding the second key
from the first, which takes several hunderd years.
 
WhenI get around to doing somesecurity stuff, I'll probably use a DES-like
algorithm, but put it back to 64 bits like it was before the NSA
shortened it so they coud|decode it.  If you truly care I'd suggest
doing txe|same.  It means youhave to do it in software|instead
ofhardware, though.

Message number 7826 is 12 lines from Phil Reed
To sysop at 09:25:11 on 01-Apr-81.
Subject: Rivest codes

To solve a Rivest code, the essential problem is to find the two
prime factors of a very large number. (200+ digits). The keys that
you keep seceret are two primes. The encoding involves doing a modulo
multiplication using the product of the primes, and decoding is
the same operation using one of the primes. (It's more involved than
that but I don't have the paper here.) The en/decode function can be
done by a multiply/shift function, which doesn't take as long as
you might think. However, as was pointed out, factoring a large
number is a non-trivial problem (it's called NP incomplete)
and finding the primes to do is not easy. A method was discussed
that in a sense developed numbers that were PROBABLY prime (a very
strange concept).                      ...phil

Message number 7859 is 20 lines from Mark Thorson
To ALL at 07:44:52 on 02-Apr-81.
Subject: PHONES ARE PASSE ...

LATE AT NIGHT AT A PUBLIC MAILBOX, THE SUSPICIOUS CHARACTER DROPS IN A
MYSTERIOUS PARCEL.  IN THIS ACT, HE HAS JOINED THE RANKS OF THOUSANDS
IN THE LATEST HIGH-TECHNOLOGY CRIME FAD -- MAIL PHREAKING!
 
THE STORY BEGINS ON COLLEGE CAMPUSES OF THE MID-1980'S WITH THE 'BROWN BOX',
AN INNOCENT-LOOKING PACKAGE EQUIPPED WITH A MECHANISM TO CHANGE THE CARD
IN ITS ADDRESS WINDOW.  BY WAITING UNTIL IT HAS PASSED THE WEIGHING AND
STAMP CANCELLATION STATIONS, IT CAN RIDE ACROSS THE COUNTRY FOR THE
PRICE OF TRAVELLING TO THE NEXT TOWN.
 
ANOTHER TOOL OF THE TRADE IS THE 'LETTER DIVERTER', AN ORDINARY MANILA
ENVELOPE WITH A SLOT CUT IN THE SIDE.  WHEN JOSTLED AMONG THE OTHER
LETTERS IN A MAILBAG, ONE INEVITABLY FALLS THROUGH.  A PIECE OF TAPE
INSIDE THE ENVELOPE OR A PAPER TRAPDOOR ATTACHED TO THE SLOT RETAINS
THE LETTER UNTIL ITS NEW DESTINATION IS REACHED.
 
PERHAPS THE MOST FAMOUS EXPLOIT OF A MAIL PHREAK IS THAT OF THE LEGENDARY
'POSTMASTER CRUNCH', WHO MAILED HIMSELF FROM LOMPOC TO HONOLULU.
HE WOULD HAVE PICKED UP A VACATION IN HAWAII FOR LESS THAN TEN DOLLARS,
IF THE ADDRESSEE HADN'T REFUSED TO PAY AN ADDITIONAL FIVE CENTS POSTAGE DUE.

Message number 7919 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To sysop at 11:46:04 on 04-Apr-81.
Subject: DES and the width of the key

If you encrypt the message by feeding it through two chips,
each of which uses an n-bit code, you can take the two codes
and interchange them through separate methods.  This reduces
the possibility that the code will be compromised, allowing
immediate access.  Compromising the code is the most dangerous.
 
However, you have not encrypted the message with a 2 x n key.
There will be some other n bit key which can decode the algor
ithm in one step.  The key has not become harder to guess or
determine by exhaustive search.
 
Two examples:
 
Consider the following chip, which accepts the message and
encodes it using the algorithm "add m to the ascii value of
each character".  This is a key which is likely to be 8 bits
of information.
 
If you pass information through two of these chips, you can
decode it with one eight-bit key (key-1 plus key-2).


Message number 7920 is 19 lines from George Burdell
To sysop at 11:58:51 on 04-Apr-81.
Subject: sysop

The same thing would happen with the DES chip.  (Otherwise, why
do you think the Government successfully prevented the chip man-
ufacturers from producing chip with twice the key width (which
would have produced a key that could not have been forcibly cracked
in a lifetime)?)
 
Second example:
 
If you have an algorithm with an n-bit key, you can split it up
into n information packets, each of which contains the binary
value of the bit it represents and its position.  Depending on
the length of the string, this position information could be
further split up, in a tree structured fashion.
 
There are an infinite number of things you can do to split up
that information and transmit it separately.  Doubling the
length of the key simply doubles the point at which this infinite
tree starts, but doesn't provide any benefits on any reasonable
algorithms.


Message number 7921 is 15 lines from George Burdell
To sysop at 12:24:47 on 04-Apr-81.
Subject: sysop

If you split a key in half, you reduce the amount of time
it takes to perform the algorithm the key describes by
2 to the n/2.
 
With a sixteen bit key, you reduce the amount of time it
takes to decode a message by a factor of 256.  (A lifetime,
maybe?)  This applies to the type of machine on which this
decoding would be done.
 
Now with half of a sixteen bit key known, (if you know its
position, that's only one more bit) you only have to perform
256 guesses instead of 65536.
 
Taking the DES key twice, you do get twice as many bits available
for transmission of the code from point A to point B.

Message number 7946 is 10 lines from JON TARA
To ALL at 14:25:49 on 05-Apr-81.
Subject: ENCRYPTATION SPECIAL ISSUE

The December, 1979 issue of ACM Computing Surveys is a special
issue of Crytology.  There are articles on public-key systems,
Encrytation and secure computer networks, and a general
update on the "state of the art".  Also many useful references.
See also July, 1979 Scientific American , July, 1979
IEEE Spectrum, Novemberr, 1978 issue of the newsletter of
the IEEE Communications society and August, 1977 Scientific
American.   These are all fairly readable, since Computing
Surveys carrier only tutorials, and the IEEE articles are tutorials
also (as opposed to in-depth slinging among the inner circle...)

this is listed next to TCBBS in Bill Blue's list!  The

Message number 8116 is 8 lines from Susan Thunder
To Mark Thorson at 00:47:32 on 10-Apr-81.
Subject: Telenet

 
To get off a host on Telenet, but still be on the Telenet system,
(Like for Host-Hopping), just type the atsign on a line by itself,
hit return, and when you get the atsign prompt type the letter D.
It will disconnect you from the host and leave you ready to con-
tinue your scan.
 
                                          THUNDER


Message number 8117 is 17 lines from Susan Thunder
To David Westerby at 00:55:42 on 10-Apr-81.
Subject: Telenet Hosts

 
The best way to find out what is on Telenet is by scanning.  Pick a
popular area code and start with 10 and go all the way to 150 or so...
Every time you hit a system, try to hack the login.  Sometimes you
can login as DEMO, or OPERATOR, or GAMES, etc.  I have been very
successful with this type of scanning.  At the @ type C AAA NN where
"C" means Collect, "AAA" is an area code, and "NN" or "NNN" is a
number between 10 and 150+.  If you get a host that you can't login
to, type @ <CR> D and it will return you to system prompt.  Telenet
no longer publishes a user-guide that lists the hosts, but it is rumoured
that there exists such a list on one of the 909 machines...909 95D is
a list of all their dial-ups.  And there is a guy that answers their
voice line (the 800 number) in the middle of the night who can be
persuaded into giving out occasionally useful tidbits of info on the
system.  Have fun.
 
                                            THUNDER

Message number 8210 is 18 lines from John Wood
To kerry abel at 13:15:20 on 12-Apr-81.
Subject: privacy of user log

I think you did not see one of my msgs.  My interest in user
log privacy was an intellectual/academic one, not a real concern
for myself.  It was sparked by Bernard's interest in DES encryption
my point (to summarize) if you g t all that trouble (des) of encrypting
msgs, don't you think the user log should be private info also?
Remember, lots of 'security'  is by implied access, for example, a
programmer writes a program that processes data.  He does not
have access to the data, that is specified by the user when the
program runs.  But the programmar can compromise the data by
writing a program that say, blinks the lights on the computer or
stops printng a report for a while when a certain type of info is
processed.  like 'if president's salary = salaray then for I=1 to 5000
do...' if the data is read, a noticeable pause in the program
execution (assumming the programmer can watch the program) indicates
effectively, the value of the data.  This is not original, I read tis
in a book on privacy/security whic I started reading after all the
accusations of Ma Bell monitoring this line, using DES, ETC.
p.s.  Did anybody ever recover those stolen floppies??

Message number 8301 is 20 lines from Susan Thunder
To ALL PHREAKS! at 19:04:43 on 15-Apr-81.
Subject: CCIS

For those of you who know what CCIS is, here is some information on
testing the trunks via the Stored Program Control Processor Channel
on the DS 40 keyboard.
The output message format is TKM00 TRK:aa-bbb cccc
Explantion--Trunk status update report.
Explanation of variable fields:
     aa-bbb=Trunk identifier, where:  aa=Trunk Register Block Index
                                                            (01-31)
                                      bbb=Trunk Register Number
                                                          (000-511)
     cccc--Specifies stimulus which caused state change, where:
 
VPCF = VPC Retest Failure
FAXF = Facility Failure
FAXR = Facility Restore
DASF = DAS Failure
DASR = DAS Restore
BLKD = Trunk Blocked
UBLK = Trunk Unblocked
HWON = Trunk on High + Wet List


Message number 8302 is 20 lines from Susan Thunder
To ALL PHREAKS! at 19:24:16 on 15-Apr-81.
Subject: CCIS CON'T

HWOF = Trunk off High + Wet List
CIOF = CIOT Test failure
ATXF = Auto Transmission Test Failure
SVST = Trunk SV Point Stuck
FLCB = False Link Controller Bid
NLCB = No Link Controller Bid
TRQM = Trunk Query Mismatch
VPCR = VPC Retest Restore
ATXR = Auto Transmission Test Restore
UQLB = Unequipped Label Signal Received
DSBL = Trunk Automatically Disabled
 
Of course some of you are surely wondering what good it does to know
what the computer-generated trouble messages mean...Well, if somebody
were to be screwing around with various CCIS commands, it is helpful to
know what the return trunking messages mean, so that one knows if one's
commands have been useful.  Note the DSBL message.  Could it be that
one's hacking efforts have been successful if this message is generated?
Pending interest in this subject, I will leave more about the CCIS
[computer] Stored Program Control and it's applications.     THUNDER

am referring to the message you left for Ms. Thunder recently,
condemning her lifestyle, her speech, and her use of this system.

even know?  Almost no one on this system knows any other person

are never called for (to quote ZORK) in a high class establishment
like this.  How do YOU know if Ms. Thunder is really that bad?  I
don't care what someone writes about me on this system.  I can only
form an opinion after meeting them.  And if I don't like them, I don't
start fouling computer systems with nonsensical comments, but tell them
myself.  Maybe that's the only way you can relate to people, by telling
them nasty things over computer systems, where you don't have to see

Message number 8443 is 20 lines from Hugh Packard
To ALL PHREAKS at 13:19:31 on 22-Apr-81.
Subject: PHONE ELECTRICAL SPECS.

HELLO THERE, PACKARD HERE,
  AND NOW FOR SOME TELEPHONE STUFF!
THE TELEPHONE HAS TWO BASIC STATES:
ON HOOK AND OFF HOOK. WHEN THE PHONE IS
ON HOOK, IT LOOKS LIKE INFINITY OHMS
TO THE INCOMING LINE. WHEN OFF HOOK,
ITS RESISTANCE DROPS TO ABOUT 660
OHMS. IF A 660 OHM, 1 WATT RESISTOR
IS CONNECTED ACROSS THE RED AND GREEN
WIRES, THE LINE LOOKS LIKE AN OFF-HOOK
PHONE IS CONNECTED TO IT.
LINE VOLTAGES:
WHEN ON HOOK, THE PHONE LINE SUPPLIES
APPROX. 48 VOLTS ACROSS THE RED AND
GREEN WIRES. WHEN RINGING STARTS, A
20 HERTZ, 45 VOLT AC SIGNAL IS
SUPERIMPOSED ON THE 48 VOLTS DC,
MAKING THE SIGNAL LOOK LIKE AC
THAT SWINGS FROM 0 TO PLUS 90 VOLTS.
--CONTINUED NEXT MESSAGE--


Message number 8444 is 20 lines from Hugh Packard
To ALL PHREAKS at 13:27:37 on 22-Apr-81.
Subject: MORE PHONE ELEC. SPECS.

...WHEN THE PHONE IS TAKEN OFF
HOOK, THE VOLTAGE ACROSS THE RED
AND GREEN WIRES IS CHANGED TO ABOUT
4 OR 6 VOLTS (I'M NOT SURE ABOUT THIS).
TELCO REFERS TO THIS VOLTAGE CHANGE
AS 'CHANGE OF BATTERY' BECAUSE THEY
ACTUALLY SWITCH IN A DIFFERENT POWER
SUPPLY.
WHEN YOU TALK ON THE PHONE, YOU
GENERATE AN AC VOLTAGE OF ABOUT 1 VOLT
SUPERIMPOSED ON THE 4 TO 6 VOLTS DC.
(AGAIN I'M NOT POSITIVE ABOUT VOLTAGES).
NOW, HERE'S A TRICK, TRY TO FOLLOW
THIS:
IF, WHILE THE PHONE IS RINGING,
THE PHONE IS TAKEN OFF HOOK FOR
ABOUT HALF A SECOND, AND PUT BACK
ON HOOK, THE RING BATTERY IS DROPPED
BUT OFF HOOK CURRENT DOESN'T HAVE
--CONTINUED--


Message number 8445 is 20 lines from Hugh Packard
To ALL PHREAKS at 13:33:56 on 22-Apr-81.
Subject: MORE PHONE ELEC. SPECS.

A CHANCE TO SET UP ON THE LINE.
WHAT HAS HAPPENED IS THE RINGING
HAS BEEN STOPPED, BUT THE PERSON
CALLING YOU IS STILL ON THE LINE!
THAT PERSON WILL STAY THERE AND
THE SWITCHING EQUIPMENT WILL THINK
YOU HAVEN'T ANSWERED AS LONG AS YOU
DON'T CONNECT 660 OHMS ACROSS THE RED
AND GREEN WIRES! NOW, WHAT YOU DO
IS CONNECT A PHONE (OR JUST A HAND
SET) ACROSS THE RED AND GREEN
THROUGH A 1 MFD CAPACITOR ON
EACH WIRE. NOW, THE AC VOICE CURRENT
PASSES THROUGH THE CAPACITORS TO
THE PHONE, BUT THE PHONE DOESN'T
LOOK OFF HOOK! YOU CAN TALK TO YOUR
FRIEND AND THE PHONE LOOKS TO THE
TELCO EQUIPMENT LIKE IT'S STILL
RINGING!
--CONTINUED--

Message number 8449 is 16 lines from Joshua Gordon
To >>ALL "RESPONSIBLE" TYPES<< at 15:33:03 on 22-Apr-81.
Subject: LANGUAGE

Ho-hum.  Regarding responsibility and other such matters,
do exactly what you want.  If I feel a need or a desire to use smutty language
I intend to.  It's hardly a matter of responsibility.  Seems to me it is more
a matter of freedom of choice.  Dirty words don't hurt anyone, far as
I can tell--and even the spectre of self-censorship rather
bothers me.  Remember EC Comics? The Comics Code, and all of the
restrictions imposed there, came about as the result of self-censorship.
As a result, creativity in comics has been rather arbitrarily restricted.
Similarly, the Hayes Office of Hollywood was the self-censoring unit
for the movies, and went way too far...possibly actually damaged the
freedom of expression in the movies until the last ten years.  If
smut offends you, you, the user, may feel free to use a system that
practices censorship.  But don't expect me or anyone else to choose
my style to meet with your sensitivities.  It doesn't work that way for
me, anyhow.  Do what thou wilt shall be the whole of the Law.  The
word of Sin is Restriction.

Message number 8463 is 11 lines from SYSOP
To Lynn Skidmore at 09:15:01 on 23-Apr-81.
Subject: Sequential msg read

Hi Lynn,
   For info on sequential msg retrieval see msg # 1161.  You can also get
info from the Help files with  H;SEQ  .  The main reason 8BBS doesn't
support the sequential retrieval mode where you are asked if you want to
read each msg is that that method is VERY slow and time consuming.  Since
this is a single user system it is important to make efficient use of
your connect time.  If you use the  R;NNNN,-  or  R;NNNN;^  format you
can always use the ^C or C to skip a msg you're not interested in.  Typing
a ^K or K get's you back to the Function: prompt.  Of course you can still
use the S or ^S - ^Q to stop and start output so you don't miss anything.
    Regards,..

Message number 8492 is 9 lines from SYSOP
To Joshua Gordon at 17:29:12 on 23-Apr-81.
Subject: 8BBS backup

Hi Joshua,
   Yes, 8BBS files are backed up.  Not because of fear of user damage
but due to realization of my own carelessness when I do msg purges.
A user does not actually delete a msg when he 'Kills' it.  All that
happens is that that msg is flagged as being 'inactive'.  It is very
easy to re-activate 'killed' messages.  A msg doesn't really get
deleted until I do a msg purge.  Sometimes I've messed up the msg purge
procedure and have lost a few msg's and scrambled the file structure so
that is the reason I make a backup.  Regards,..

Message number 8496 is 7 lines from George Burdell
To Hugh Packard at 21:01:48 on 23-Apr-81.
Subject: Electrical Characteristics

There is not a physical change of the battery across the line.
"Change in Battery" is short for change in the measurement of
the battery.
 
The C.O. is providing a constant current source of about
55 ma.  So as you vary the resistance across the line, the
voltage will vary but the current remains fairly constant.

Message number 8535 is 7 lines from SYSOP
To Bill Bell at 19:19:41 on 25-Apr-81.
Subject: Password Problems

Hi Bill,
   Some info about the optional 8BBS login access password.  It is changed
with the "U" function.  It is only four characters.  When entering the
password the case must also match.  If you keep this info in mind, you'll
find that using the password is a bit easier.  If you still haven't
managed to get the password entered properly after four tries, the system
will log you off.

Message number 8538 is 19 lines from George Burdell
To Steven Inness at 11:04:14 on 26-Apr-81.
Subject: A bit more on 212 / Vadic dif's

The differences in modulation technique between the Bell 212
and the Vadic 3405 give rise to an important operating difference:
 
With the Vadic operating in "High-Speed" mode, speaking to another
VADIC, data may be transmitted at any speed up to 1200 bps.  The
high-speed frequencies are used even if the data is at 300, so a
normal 300 baud modem can't talk these frequencies.
 
With the 212 operating in high-speed mode, the data better really
be at 1200, otherwise it won't get sent correctly.
 
The Vadic 3451 incorporates ALL THREE modulation techniques.  It
can automatically answer with any one of the three (the "HS" switch
is ignored when answering).  When originating, the "HS" switch will
determine whether to start up with the low-speed frequencies or to
try both the Bell and the Vadic High-Speed frequencies.  (You can
end up with two Vadic 3451s handshaking at the Bell frequencies
rather than the Vadic freqs depending on the timing of when you
throw the originate switch.

Message number 8577 is 20 lines from Susan Thunder
To Joshua Gordon at 05:35:43 on 28-Apr-81.
Subject: Magick by the Page

Dear Joshua;
     There was once a time in my life when I was asked to assist
somebody with something because of my "vibes".  I was having a drink
at a club called the Rainbow in Hollywood (this was in '77) and this
guy comes up to me and says, "Jimmy Page would like to have the star
you are wearing."  Of course my reaction was something like "What kind
of bullshit is this guy laying on me??"  The star, by the way, was
on a chain around my neck:  I had bought it in a curiosity shop on
Santa Monica Blvd.  It was sterling silver, had 7 points, and I had
engraved the word "THUNDER" on it.  I wore it constantly, never taking
it off because I thought it brought me good luck.  (This was before I
had been initiated into anything)...So I tell this guy that if Jimmy 
Page wants my star, then he's going to have to come over and get it
himself.  He did.
     And we sat and talked for a few minutes.  Avoiding alot of details
that have no pertinence to the topic at hand, I was introduced to
Crowley and his theories/philosophies.  I was invited to participate
in a ritual celebrating the vernal equinox.  And, apparently, my perfor-
mance must not have been up to par because that was the end of that.
                                                 THUNDER

Subject: What is it about this system?

Hi Mark, & others,
   There have been several quieries lately by users asking how to do
"keyword" or selective searches.  Is there some sort of psychological
revulsion associated with the word "HELP" or the "H" character?  Or
perhaps users immediately change to 'EXPERT' mode when they know very
little aobut the system and thereby miss many of the prompts that offer
information?
    How is it possible for so many people who seem to have played
ADVENTURE to lose their curiosity when on 8BBS?  Are they afraid to
experiment?  8BBS software is quite robust and is not likely to 'crash'
if a user enters unexpected input.
 
P.S. 8BBS does indeed have selective search and/or retrieve.

Message number 8678 is 17 lines from Dan Lemberg
To Phil Reed at 16:13:15 on 30-Apr-81.
Subject: 1200 BAUD ON ARPA

Phil,
  To set arpanet baud rate, do the
following:
 
            baud rate
            ---------
@D R 178     110
     308     150
     373     300
     438     600
     503    1200
     568    1800
     633    2400
     754    110 in 9600 out
 
Hope this helps,
            Dan

Message number 8722 is 11 lines from Eric Moyer
To Richard Beal at 22:11:06 on 02-May-81.
Subject: CRT to TV

Well, there is no reason why you couldn't connect the video
output to a TV, but (is I remember correctly) the vt100 is
80 column, so that the characters would be almost totally
garbaged on the TV because a standard TV only has a bandwidth
thru the tuner of about 3 MHz, and for 80 column, you need
at least 10 MHz. About the smallest you can use with a TV
is 40 columns.  There is no reason you can't try it tho, but
I wouldn't go buy a RF mod. for just that purpose, it would
most likely turn out a waste of money...
                                        Regards...
                                          Eric

Message number 8745 is 7 lines from SYSOP
To Paul Traina at 22:46:38 on 03-May-81.
Subject: Paul Traina

Hi Paul,
   You didn't specify what size dynamic RAM's you plan on using.  You could
check out the INTEL refresh controller chip or the AMD refresh controller
IC.  I don't recall the IC numbers, just call them (or a distributor/rep)
and ask them for what you need.  Dynamic RAM's do have some drawbacks
compared to statics, but they are much less costly and if you design it
properly the refresh doesn't get in the way.  Regards,..


Message number 8746 is 16 lines from SYSOP
To Bob Kohler at 22:54:55 on 03-May-81.
Subject: 1200 baud chaos

Hi Bob,
   I am aware of 4 different 1200 baud transmission 'standards'.  These are:
 
- BELL 202  half duplex only
- BELL 212  half duplex (not sure how it differs from 202)
- VADIC 3400 full duplex
- NOVATION 1200 full duplex
 
   The above 4 types are mutually exclusive.  Meaning that none of the above
can be understood by any of the others.  VADIC makes several models that
automaticly detect either 212 or VADIC mode and use the appropriate mode.
   I believe that the BELL 212 is the most widely used (not the best, tho).
   I expect that when 8BBS eventually gets 1200 baud, it will be the B
BELL 212 'standard'.
   What I'd really like is the new Hayes "Smart Modem" if it could handle
1200 baud...  Maybe next year..  Regards,..

Message number 8752 is 11 lines from Phil Reed
To sysop at 06:51:23 on 04-May-81.
Subject: bell 212

Just wanted to point out that Bell 212 is FULL duplex 1200 baud both
ways.
       Standard voice grade lines can support up to (with luck) 2400
baud, which can be divided any number of ways (2400 baud half duplex,
1200 baud full duplex, or 1800 baud computer->terminal:150 baud
terminal->computer, to name three.)
 
oh, also, I believe that Vadic 3400 is 1200 baud full duplex as well.
The Vadic Triple modem will detect 103, 212, or 3400 and switch into
the proper mode.
                                               ...phil

Message number 8788 is 10 lines from SYSOP
To Mark Thorson at 17:24:14 on 05-May-81.
Subject: RK is OK

Hi Mark,
   My old RK05 has held up very well.  I did replace a temperature
sensitive IC in the data separator about 2 years ago.  Have had no
mechanical problems at all.  The absolute filter has to be changed
about every year (costs about $80).  Head crashes are rare if the
packs are not left on dusty floors.  The servo adjustments need to
be trimmed every year since the values drift as the transducer bulb
light output changes with age.  Head alignment could be a problem
if you want to exchange packs.  You really need a special alignment
pack to do the job right.  Regards,..

Message number 8820 is 19 lines from Mark Thorson
To INFILTRAITORS at 16:50:31 on 06-May-81.
Subject: GETTING TO KNOW TOPS-20

A 'FEATURE' OF TOPS-20 (DEC OP SYS FOR DEC-20 SERIES) IS THAT
THE COMMAND 'FINGER' USUALLY WORKS WITHOUT LOGGING IN.
IT USUALLY GIVES THE FULL NAME (I.E. MARK R. THORSON) OF EACH
LOGGED IN USER.  A TYPICAL STRATEGY HERE IS TO CALL SUCH A
SYSTEM DURING PEAK USAGE HOURS, AND DO A 'FINGER'.  SINCE LOGIN NAMES
ARE GENERALLY LAST NAMES, YOU CAN GENNERALLY THROW THE FIRST
NAME OR INITIALS AGAINST IT AS A PASSWORD:
  @LOGIN THORSON
  PASSWORD: MARK
    OR
  PASSWORD: MRT
THESE MACHINES ARE VERY COMMON. SRI-KL ON THE ARPANET IS A
GOOD EXAMPLE.  A CERTAIN MACHINE WHOSE DIALUP IS GIVEN ON THE
BERKELEY CONFERENCE TREE (408) 526-7733 IS
AN EVEN BETTER EXAMPLE (SORRY, I WILL ONLY SAY THE COMPUTER IS IN PALO ALTO).).
I RECOMMEND PULLING THE NAMES OFF AT ABOUT 3PM
LOCAL TIME, AND DIALING BACK AFTER 5PM (WHEN PEOPLE HAVE GONE HOME).
EVEN LATER MIGHT BE ADVISABLE (SAY, 8PM).  I WOULD BE AMUSED BY
REPORTS OF ANY SUCCESSES RESULTING FROM THIS LETTER.

Message number 8834 is 20 lines from LEN FREEDMAN
To SUSAN THUNDER at 22:56:40 on 06-May-81.
Subject: THE VIRGIN

THE JUDEAO-CHRISTIAN SYSTEM OF RELIGIONS HOLDS THAT GOD STARTED WITH
NOTHING IN THE UNIVERSE--JUST A TREMENDOUS VACUUM. HE SIMPLY 'THOUGHT
UP' THE WORLD & THE HEAVENS ETC. SURELY A BEING WHO COULD DO THIS COULD
'THINK' A WOMAN PREGNANT!  NOT BEING A CHRISTIAN, I'M NOT OBLIGATED TO
BELIEVE THAT EVERY WORD OF THE BIBLE IS 'GOSPEL' TRUTH, BUT RATHER I
BELIEVE THAT THESE STORIES HAVE VALUE IN WHAT WE CAN LEARN FROM THEM.
WHETHER OR NOT JESUS WAS BORN OF A VIRGIN (& SOME CHRISTIANS DON'T BELIEVE IT
EITHER) IS NOT IMPORTANT--IT'S JESUS'S PERSONALITY & TEACHING THAT MATTER.
THE ANCIENT GREEKS BELIEVED THAT ZEUS TOOK THE FORM OF A SWAN AND SEDUCED
LEDA TO BEAR BACCUS (ANOTHER MAN-GOD, GOD OF DRINKING AND CONVIVIALITY).
THE MUSEUMS OF EUROPE ARE FULL OF PICTURES OF A BIG, PLUMP, RENAISSANCE-LOOKING
WOMAN HAVING SEX WITH A SWAN (IN SOME OF THEM LYING DOWN, IN SOME OF THEM
STANDING UP, ETC.). I DON'T THINK THE ANCIENT GREEKS REALLY BELIEVED THIS
STORY, BUT IT HELPED EXPLAIN ABOUT THE PROCESS OF FERMENTATION AND THE
PROPER USE OF WINE. 
  THERE WAS A CASE IN AUSTRALIA SOME YEARS AGO WHERE A GIRL WHO WAS
A GYNECOLOGICALLY-PROVABLE VIRGIN GOT PREGNANT & IT WAS FINALLY ATTRIBUTED
TO LOOSE SPERM IN THE COMMUNITY SWIMMING POOL. BUT AREN'T WE KIND OF SPLIT-
TING HAIRS? I MEAN DOES THAT SHOOT DOWN THE WHOLE BIBLE? THERE'S GOOD STUFF
IN IT TOO, I THINK.     LEN

Message number 8895 is 20 lines from Tim Bessie
To Religionists at 00:45:15 on 08-May-81.
Subject: My opinion

Well, I am back after a long absence, in which I was doing much work.
I have strong opinions about religion.  I do not actively campaign
'against' religion, but I will criticize a religion that trys to push
its values upon others.  Christianity seems to be formost in this,
which is why I reject it more than any other religion.  If god (notice
the small 'g') is supposedly so wonderful, how can a 'good christian'
explain all the horrible deeds done in the name of Chrisitanity? i.e.
the slaughtering of the Hougonauts, persecution of the jews, torturing
of the various indian tribes and eastern peoples, etc.  These were
actually done for political and greedy reasons, but under the guise of
'Christianity."  That is how the christian religion gained so
much power... it provided an excellent medium for the growth of ignorance,
violence, and greed.  Many of the eastern and tribal religions, although
strict, held the conviction that men and nature, as well as personal
honor, were more important than money and power.  Education was
put formost, and profit was held at a lower value than in Christian nations.
     As for my ideas about the exsistance of some 'supreme being', I
am extremely doubtful.  Even a 'life force' has yet to be proven.  I
work on proven facts, and not on a twisted faith passed down through
ages by (cont)


Message number 8896 is 20 lines from Tim Bessie
To Religionists at 00:52:16 on 08-May-81.
Subject: cont.

senile old men who could not remember history properly.
     In a historical perspective, religious writings have very little
value that I have seen.  Their mythological value, however, is
high, and describes that philosophy of the people from which it came.
The bible is just as valid as the Book of the Dead, the Elder Edda
(the Norse 'bible'), and the various legends of the European
Teutonic tribes.  Personally, I find the Norse and European myths
much more colorful and interesting than the ones brought back from
the 'holy' lands.
     Worship of a diety provides material to fill a gap in
people's lives.  However, any group of people could be just
as fulfilled if they considered knowledge and facts, rather than
ancient legends, as more important and worthy of study.  This would
fill the void in their lives caused by their ignorance.  All around them
they see things beginning and ending.  So it is natural that they want to
have a beginning and an ending, as well as simple answers to their
qustions, about their own existance.  If a society would search for
facts, instead of accepting stories made up to satisfy their curiosity without
having to do any work, they would find life much more enjoyable,
interesting, and rewarding.            -Tim Bessie

Message number 8906 is 17 lines from Joshua Gordon
To Software pirates at 11:23:54 on 08-May-81.
Subject: Piracy

I agree completely with Tim Binder.  The profit margin in writing game
software (as opposed to operating software) is remarkably small,
considering the time and energy that goes into it. If I work my ass off
to write a program, expecting to be able to make some money off of it
(and I should be able to, shouldn't I?  I am an artist, and should be
able to reap the rewards of my work!!) it is completely unfair for 
you to deny me my just reward.  The only payoff (after the joy of 
programming is finished) of the work is the royalties.  I think that
freeloading software is reprehensible, and there is no ethical 
justification for it.  IT HURTS THE WRITER, plain and simple.  I also
don't buy pirated albums, or videotapes, if the art is available for
sale.  Folks--if you want to be fair to the one person hurt by your
software theft, you don't have to pay the $30-$40 bucks, maybe, but
at least you might consider sending a dollar or two to the author.  There
is not yet a standard royalty for software authors, but usually that
is about what the author gets--the rest is for distribution, publicity,
and profit for the company.  Dig?

Message number 8960 is 19 lines from SYSOP
To Tom Watson at 23:41:37 on 09-May-81.
Subject: Why no "marked messages"?

There have been several recent comments left complaining about the lack of
"marked message" retrieval.  There are several reasons why 8BBS does not
have that 'feature'.
  8BBS software is modeled after CBBS software and as such, endeavors to
maintain some semblance of similarity.  The "marked message" retrieval
method is usually associated with ABBS, PMS or Conn-80 type BBS's.
  Perhaps the main reason 8BBS does not support "marked messages" is that
I personally do not think it is particularly well implemented in that it
requires the user to quickly type a 'marking' char at just the right time
in order to later retrive "marked messages".
  I think 8BBS has something better.   This is the selective Retrieval
capability.  It is documented in the HELP files, but it allows a user to
selectively retrieve messages with the same type of command format as used
with a selective summary.  In fact, there is no need to ever use the  S
command, since selective or sequential Retrieval combines the functions of
the Q, S and R functions.  Just use the ^C or C character to skip messages
you are NOT interested in.  The ^K or K character gets you back to the
Function: menu.  Why not check out the HELP file and try it sometime.
  Regards,..

just a note, ( i usually stay out of these arguments)
someone raised the point how can you really put much stock in a
bunch of tales (the bible) that was passed through the eons and
got mangled and changed along the way etc.
well, the FACTUAL point i want to make is this:
Not to long ago (in our current lifetimes) a bunch of clay jars
were discovered in a cave by a small body of water known as the
Red Sea.  The 'RED SEA' scrolls were a collection of manuscripts
(written on fan-fold continuous lamb-gut printout paper
no doubt) of which a majority were copies of the old testament
and other books of the bible.  The amazing thing about this
discovery was the fact that they were the oldest known copy
yet to be found (verified by reliable carbon-14 tracing.)
that is the archeological significance, the religious
enlightenment was the fact that the text of the bible and other
documents matched 'current' versions exactly.  Thus, hard
evidence seems to prove that the bible has remained unchaged
til this day.  So, it gave a strong credence to the non-human
divine inspiration view about the source of the bible

Message number 9000 is 16 lines from Joshua Gordon
To Phil Reed at 11:42:01 on 11-May-81.
Subject: Ackermann's Function

Ackermann's function can be stated a couple of ways.  Here they are:
  
       A(0,n,p) = n + p
       A(1,0,p) = 0
       A(m+2,0,p) = 1
 
       and
 
       A(m+1,n+1,p) = A(m,A(m+1,n,p),p)
 
       You might want to do it more specifically (without p) as
               A(0,n) = n+1; A(1,0) = 0; A(m+2,0) = 1;
               A(m+2,n+1) = A(m,A(m+1,n))
 
       Another way of stating the thing is--whoops, not gonna have room, see
next...


Message number 9001 is 16 lines from Joshua Gordon
To Phil Reed at 11:47:27 on 11-May-81.
Subject: Cont...

Another way of stating Ackermann is:
 
       A(m,n) :=
               if m = 0 then n + 1
               else if n = 0 then (if m = 1 then 0 else 1)
               else A(m-1,A(m,n-1)).
 
       By the way, this function blows up really fast, depending upon
the value you pick for m and n (and p, if you use it).  It is the most
frequently used example of a function which is general recursive but not
primitive recursive (if you dig computation theory jabber). Source for
this is Ralston and Meek's "Encyclopedia of Computer Science", a good
general reference for all sorts of things, like number systems, random
number generators, history and trivia.  F'rinstance: KLUDGE: "an ill-
sorted collection of poorly matching parts, forming a distressing
whole."  --jpg 93

Message number 9039 is 10 lines from SYSOP

Subject: Either way its gone

Hi Mark,
   Thanks for the comments regarding 'non-existent messages'.  Yes, alternate
wording could be used, but the end result for the user is indeed that the
'message does not exist'.   The 'message does not exist' can occur if the
requested msg has actually been purged from the system or if the message is
just flagged as 'killed' or if it is a RP msg to someone else.  There is a 
bug with RP msg's that we hope to have fixed for ver 6.1   If you use a 
system access PW'd you should be able to read RP msg's that you enter, but
ver 6.0 won't let you read them 'til you log in again, we also hope to have
212A 1200 baud support soon.  Regards,..

Message number 9041 is 16 lines from Phil Reed

Subject: theft

I suggest that you read msg 8651 after this. Although that msg applies to
people raiding computer systems, I suggest that the same thoughts can be
applied to those who *STEAL* software. There is no other word for what
you do. Some people have invested many thousands of hours into development
of those programs, (don't forget, programmers earn about $10-$20/hour 
these days) and then we have to deal with people like you who go around
ripping them off by copying their stuff and passing it out. Calling
it "piracy" (cute name, huh?) doesn't change what you're doing.
It's people like you who make life misrable for the honest users of
those uncopyable software packages, when we can't make backup copies
without breaking the law.
       I suppose that I could make brownie points by turning you in,
(did you know that unauthorized copying of software is worth a $10,000
fine?) but I'd rather let you reconcider your habits.
                                                                       
                                                       thief


Message number 9042 is 11 lines from Phil Reed
To joshua gordon at 05:33:41 on 13-May-81.
Subject: oh, my acking back

Well, I tried your functions, and it degenerates into returning 1 after
about A(3,0). I don't know what I'm doing wrong, but it can't be far
off. The function I was using before was generating numbers in the 
correct range, it's just that (I thought) they weren't right.
Here's the old one:
       Ack(m,n):= if m=0 then ack:=n+1
                         else if n=0 then ack:=ack(m-1,1)
                                     else ack:=ack(m-1,ack(m,n-1))
which as you note, is NOT the same thing. For m=3,n=0..3, this function
gives ack(m,n):=5,13,29,61. Maybe if you got a version running, you
could check these numbers.             ...phil

THE DOCTRINE OF 'FAIR USE' -- THAT COPYING OF COPYRIGHTED MATERIAL

CONDITIONS (E.G. VIDEOTAPING A TEEVEE SHOW, PLAYING A BEATLES' SONG
ON YOUR GUITAR, ETC.).

Message number 9052 is 20 lines from Joshua Gordon
To Mark Thorson at 13:32:03 on 13-May-81.
Subject: A--HOLES

I'm not particularly offended by David Lee's offers.  I also don't think
that the courts (if they matter, I'm not concerned with the legalities,
only the manners) would consider trading software to be "not for profit".
At any rate, I don't like being called an asshole.  And I don't consider
myself one, and I would appreciate name-calling be reserved for those
people who have done something to deserve it.
       As a professional software engineer (though not involved in 
any individual enterpreneuring), and as an author, I am keenly aware
of the problems involved in the theft of one's labor.  I would rather see
a dialog on the matter of software piracy, rather than a battle of
nastiness.  I guess I did get a little carried away by calling Mr.
Lee any names at all (what did I say besides "thief"?  I don't even 
remember if I said anything). If so, sorry--but the basis for my
argument remains.  I ask again--would Mr. Lee steal from a blind man?
How is that ethically any different from software piracy?  Does the 
simplicity of the means justify the action? Do what thou wilt shall
be the whole of the Law.  Were I in the market for selling custom
software, it indeed would be restricted by people giving it away for
free.  If I'm going to set myself in business as a whore, I think I
have the right to complain about free nookie, no? On my corner?

Message number 9057 is 17 lines from Marc Mosko
To All free callers! at 16:30:18 on 13-May-81.
Subject: SPC & MCI

     WEll, for all of you who don't get TAP (And you SHOULD!),
there is an artical in there that says that SPC, MCI &
Ma Bell have joined togeather.  What they have done (Please note
that all this info is from TAP # 67) was to make all the
SPC & MCI dial-ups "trap" numbers.  What this means is that every
time someone calls them, a card with YOUR phone #, time, what phone #
called,etc. gets printed out from the Ma Bell computer, and put
in storage so if MCI or SPC has a complaint about billing, Ma Bell
knows WHERE TO GO!      
        So BEWARE!   I don't know when this took effect, or when
it will, or if ever, but I would give this serious thought!

                                      Marc Mosko

P.S.  The only safe way might be to use a pay phone, but thats no good
for BBSs unless you have a LYNX pocket terminal!!!



Message number 9058 is 12 lines from Marc Mosko
To All you phreaks at 16:34:42 on 13-May-81.
Subject: An alternative to RED boxs..

A few days ago, I recieved a call from someone.  He called from
a payphone, but didn't put in enought coinage, so the operator came
on the line.  I noticed that when he dropped the coins in, not only
could the operator hear them, but so could I!  NOw, I haven't tried
this, but it seems that if you tape recorded
this (arrange to have a friend call you, etc.), you could use that tape
insted of a RED BOX!
     If this would not work, someone please tell us fast so no one
gets busted, but it sounds as if it would work, and I can see no
reason why not (then again, I don't know the interworks of the payphone
to well)..
                             Marc MOsko

TOLERATION. IT'S PRACTICALLY IMPOSSIBLE FOR A PERSON OR GROUP OF
PEOPLE TO THINK THEY HAVE "THE TRUTH" WITHOUT THEM COMING TO THINK THAT
THIS TRUTH IS ENTRUSTED TO THEM AND THAT THEIR TRUTH IS MORE CONCRETE OR
MORE ETERNAL OR JUST BETTER THAN SOMEONE ELSE'S. CHRISTIANS (OR ANYONE)
WILL TELL YOU THAT PRIDE IS THE WORST SIN OF ALL, AND YET THERE IS A
FORM OF INSIDIOUS SPIRITUAL PRIDE THAT IS RAMPANT IN SOME OF THE EVAN-
GELISTIC TYPES. I CAN HARDLY BELIEVE THAT THERE ARE PEOPLE IN THIS
COUNTRY THAT WANT TO TEACH THE BIBLICAL THEORY OF CREATION AS "SCIENTIFIC
FACT"! IF I WERE JUST AN AGNOSTIC IT WOULDN'T BOTHER ME AS MUCH AS IT DOES.
BUT I KNOW THAT RELIGION HAS ITS GOOD SIDE, AND, IN FACT, BELIEF SEEMS
TO WORK WONDERFULLY IN SOME PEOPLE. I SUSPECT THAT IT'S ORGANIZED RELIGION
THAT'S THE CULPRIT. SECTARIANISM. NONE OF THIS STUFF WOULD HAPPEN IF WE
ALL HAD OUR OWN LITTLE PERSONAL RELIGION & DIDN'T GANG UP ON EACH OTHER.
NOBODY WOULD BE TAKING CREDIT FOR ELECTING A PRESIDENT & PRESIDENTS WOULDN'T
BE PRETENDING "CHRISTIAN" VIRTUES TO GET ELECTED. WE WOULDN'T HAVE NUTS
TRYING TO LEGISLATE MORALITY & THERE WOULD BE NO 700 CLUB (THAT IN
ITSELF WOULD BE AN IMPROVEMENT!)
