Message number 9085 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To Steven Inness at 19:21:42 on 14-May-81.
Subject: Modem

The Bell 212 (as has been explained here many times before) is a
0-300 or a 1200 baud modem, depending on the way it handshakes at
the initial call.  The originator throws a switch to indicate
high speed BEFORE going into data mode.  The answer modem can figure
this out and goes into the right mode.  [The VADIC triple takes the
high speed two steps further.  1. It can automatically figure out
when in HS mode whether the other end is a 212 or a VADIC.  2. When
in HS VADIC mode, it is 0-1200.]
 
Note that with the Bell Modem you have to get your computer to
either AUTO-BAUD or sample one of the lines from the modem to
figure out what speed you are... you can't dial in at 300 and
tell the computer to switch to 1200.  You can with the VADIC if
you handshake in VADIC HS mode.  (Note that two VADIC triples
will occasionally handshake in Bell HS Mode, and are then stuck
to 1200, just as if they really were 212s.)
 
I'm not sure, but I suspect that the 212 is PSK.  It actually
runs some sort of synchronous stuff with your async data super-
imposed; which is partly why it runs at exactly 1200 only.


Message number 9086 is 19 lines from George Burdell
To Marc Mosko at 19:27:29 on 14-May-81.
Subject: RED BOX via Tape recorder

A tape of the Coin sounds is about a susceptible to getting caught
as a Red Box itself, and maybe slightly more so.
 
Red Boxers get caught mostly by three methods:
 
       1. If they are foolish enough to repeatedly use the
          same payphone, Bell Security will stake it out because
          of the receipts coming up short.
 
       2. If they are sloppy with feeding the tones into the
          phone, the operators will get suspicious and cause
          the big eyes of all the ex-FBI Bell Security people
          to go to work.  THIS IS MORE LIKELY TO HAPPEN WITH
          A TAPE RECORDER BECAUSE YOU ARE SPENDING LESS MONEY...
 
       3. They are usually doing something else, too, which gets
          eyes working on them.
 
Good luck, and don't get caught.


Message number 9087 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To Timothy Binder at 19:33:35 on 14-May-81.
Subject: Why Bell Security cares

Bell security wants to stop the people who are ripping off
their competitors because they feel that they are getting
ripped off, too.  Since the call was placed from point A to
point B by someone not authorized to use j-random-Bell-com-
petitor's service, Bell should have been getting the money.
 
I know of a case where General Telephone successfully prose-
cuted and got a conviction for someone who was ripping off
some OTHER COMPANY (not another common carrier) without much
help from the ripped-off company, because Gen-Tel, too, was
an injured party for having lost the regular long distance
business.
 
I actually read the indictment -- all the phone companies
involved got their money for the service which had been
PHYSICALLY provided, but Gen-Tel felt they had been ripped
off because they didn't get the revenue for the service
which had LOGICALLY been provided.
 
Good luck, and don't run into Security at the wrong time.

Message number 9089 is 8 lines from SYSOP
To Marc Mosko at 21:19:11 on 14-May-81.
Subject: 212A and file size

Hi Marc,
   You've been using the 212A for the past week, so you can see that it
doesn't prevent low speed users from accessing the system.  It only goes
into 1200 baud mode when it hears an originating 212 type modem.
   There are about 13,600 OS/8 blocks (256 12 bit words/block) on-line
as hard disk (RK05's), but the 8BBS message data file only takes 1100
blocks and it is usually about 50% to 80% full.
   Regards,..


Message number 9090 is 13 lines from SYSOP
To All 1200 baud users at 22:25:56 on 14-May-81.
Subject: 8BBS supports 212A 1200 baud

8BBS #1 now supports the 212A 1200 baud transmission mode.  If you have a
modem that is compatible with the 212A you can now use 8BBS at 1200 baud.
 
NOTE: The 212A is NOT compatible with the 202, VADIC, or NOVATION 1200
      baud transmission modes.
 
If you log on at 1200, don't use the 'A' function to alter the baud rate
because the 212A can't change to low speed.  High or Low speed mode is
determined by the originating modem when the call is connected to the 212A
answer modem.
 
If you have problems while using the 1200 baud mode, please let us know.
We don't have another 212A to check it out, so we are relying on your info.


Message number 9091 is 19 lines from SYSOP
To All 600 baud users at 22:57:20 on 14-May-81.
Subject: 8BBS supports 600 baud?

Going all out this evening...  Did some testing at 600 baud and find that
the 212A seems to do about as well at 600 baud as some acoustic couplers
do at 300 baud.  At least it appears that way when I call from the other
line in the kitchen...  The old Novation 4103B had a MUCH higher error
rate when used at 600 baud.  I tried sending a full 80 char line of each
printing char and found that the error rate (for me) is less than 2%.
I was able to dump the full 'O' list with NO errors, which tends to indicate
that the 212A is sending 600 baud OK.  I suspect that the major cause of
errors is due to the AJ acoustic coupler not being able to originate very
well at 600.
   If you have a PMMI or DC HAYES direct connect modem, and are a local
caller, you may find that 600 baud will work well.  Currently, 8BBS does
NOT support 600 baud at login.  The 'A' function allows you to select 600
baud.  We are very interested in learning if you find 600 baud operation
worthwhile with the 212A.  If you find that 600 baud works OK for you,
please let us know, also let us know if you'd like 8BBS to recognize 600
baud at login.  This would mean that 8BBS would start the 'auto-baud'
"Press RETURN:" loop at 600 baud, wait for a char, if not a CR, then try
at 300, then 150, 110, then back to 600 again.   <cont'd next msg>

Message number 9103 is 20 lines from Phil Reed
To mark thorson at 11:22:16 on 15-May-81.
Subject: re: your comments: stealing software

Rather than let you put words in my mouth, I'll take up the challange.
There IS a fundemental diffrence between reading messages left here for
others, and copying propritary software and passing it around. I'm
suprised that you could logically connect the two. To start with, you
do have the option to keep random people from reading comments directed
to a specific person. If you choose not to exercise that option, you are
specifically allowing anyone to read that msg who wants to. That is the
whole basis of these public msg systems. These are, after all, BULLETIN
BOARDS. This one is more sophisticated than most, precisely because it
allows you to not let me read messages that you have left *IF* *YOU*
*WANT* *TO*.
       As for Mr. Lee, he may or may not be a thief in the eyes of the
law. That would depend on if he was passing out copies of the software
that he had bought. If he was passing on copies of software that somebody
had given to him, then legally he is in a gray area, however, (and this
is the important point) he is still *MORALLY* a thief. If he did not pay for
the copies of the software he is passing around, then he could be convicted
for recieving stolen property, and more importantly, if he passes copies of
the illegal copy around, he is *STILL* ripping of the authors of the
program. As far as I am concerned, (remember, this is me talking)..more..

..if he really needs the software (say visicalc), then he can afford to
go out and buy it. If he can't afford it, then he probably doesn't need

       The reason that the large IBM installations don't have this problem
(and therefore the reason that we can't talk about them the same way we
can talk about the Apple software) is because you really can't do anything
with just the software; you need to make a multi-million dollar
investment to use it. Being able to back up your software for the IBM
is just a important as for the apple, but the situations are diffrent.
(Not morally though, as you could send a copy of something to your friend
in the next computer room down the street. That's just as bad.)
       It's people like you and Mr. Lee, with the attitude that if you
can get at it, you can do anything you like and everyone else can go
to hell, that are causing the rest of us so much grief.
 
                                       wise up.

Subject: NSA and Telco

Hi David,
   Just received my latest issue of "Crypologia".  In an article on the
Public Cryptography Study Group I noticed the following quote that might
be of interest to you.
   'Cryptographic researchers and some other academics see in the NSA's efforts
a severe threat to their personal freedom as well as to their professional 
work.  "We're entering a stage of computerization where the use of computers is
threatening whatever privacy we have," said George Davida of the Univ. of
Wisc. and Georgia Inst. of Tech., who is one of the leading opponents of prior
review (by NSA).  "Telephone networks are computer networks in fact," Davida
said.  "There are opportunities for abuse in telephone companies in electronic
mail and EFT. All these introduce new techniques for invading privacy that we
didn't have before.  We have to consider all of these applications along with
NSA's mission to determine whether it's worth giving up a large chunk of free-
dom in return for whatever messages we may be able to intercept worldwide."
  Although the NSA will not say specifically what has raised its eyebrows,
knowledgeable observers in the field say recent papers on so-called public
key crypto-systems, which are important to the US code system, have made the
agency particularly jittery.

Message number 9124 is 16 lines from fred fin
To ALL at 01:39:45 on 16-May-81.
Subject: tape recording coins in pay phones

You are correct, Marc Mosco, taping the coins in a pay phone works very
well.  We did it a few years ago, in school.  A direct tap to your home 
phone line works best; use an audio transformer and a 1 microfarad 
capacitor in series with the line (to keep the d.c. out).  Try to use a good
reel-to-reel tape deck, then make dubs to a cassette recorder.  Have a 
friend call you from a pay phone, and deposit the money as you record.
    When he hangs up, all but the original dime will come back.  
If you don't have a direct tap, use a phone pick-up (one of those suction
cup thingies) positioned on the earpiece for minimum hum pick-up.  Your
friend should pause between depositing coins, to make it easier to cue up
the tape later.
 
The coins values are as follows - 5 cents, one beep
                                -10 cents, two beeps
                                -25 cents, five fast beeps
That is, a beep per nickle of money. Quarters are faster, to save time.


Message number 9125 is 7 lines from fred fin
To ALL at 01:49:52 on 16-May-81.
Subject: Playing tape recordings into pay phones

Playing a tape of the beep sounds money makes in a pay phone is an effective
alternative to building a red box.  Some thoughts on this follow:
A good order to have money on the tape is one nickel, one dime, then a long
($5-$7 worth) string of quarters.  Have a two or three second pause between
each coin sound.  Then simply start the tape at the correct place to get the
correct change.  



Message number 9126 is 20 lines from fred fin
To ALL at 02:05:14 on 16-May-81.
Subject: Cautions on playing recordings into pay

There are a few things to avoid when beating a pay phone with a tape recorder.
 
Have the tape properly cued up ahead of time, so you won't start it in the
middle of a beep.  This is most embarrassing.  Use an earphone for privacy.
 
Use an external speaker to hold up to the mouthpeice so the operator won't
hear the noise of starting the cassette recorder.
 
Try not to play too much money in, the operator will want to "return" your
money and have you "redeposit" it.  If you are paying before the call, just
tell her you will talk just that much extra.  If you "pay" too much 
after the call, she will want to mail you the extra.  Watch the name and 
address you give here.  It is really suspicious to tell here to keep the 
change.  I don't think the phone company likes it.
 
ALWAYS use a real dime or nickle first.  There is a coin sensor in the
phone that must detect the first coin or the operator will know you are fishy.
 
Always be super nice to the operator, and helpful.  They will do anything for
you if you are nice to them.

Subject: The most important tip of all

 
                The most important tip of all:
 
                Practice, Practice, Practice
 
Make a real long distance call from a payphone, and talk longer
than three minutes so you will have to put more in at the end.
Do this with real money.  Now you know the format, practice it by
calling another pay phone and having your friend at that end play
operator, asking you to deposit an amount.  Then he can listen to you
doing it to see how good you are.
 
Spend a dollar now instead of paying a lawyer later.
 
Also a note: There a two differnt kinds of pay phone beeps. 
One uses a pure tone for the beeps, the other uses two mixed tones.
You must be careful to know what kind of pay phone you are calling from,
and use the correct recording for that phone.  Listen real carefully
when you deposit your first dime and you will hear the beep in the
backround.

Message number 9140 is 20 lines from Mark Thorson
To BART RIDERS & PHREAKS at 15:21:38 on 16-May-81.
Subject: COUNTERFEIT CARDS

FOR YOU OUT-OF-TOWNERS, BART IS THE BAY-AREA-RAPID-TRANSIT SYSTEM.
IT IS AN ULTRA-MODERN AND HIGHLY UNRELIABLE RAILWAY SYSTEM SERVING
THE SAN FRANCISCO AND EAST BAY AREAS.
 
ENTRY INTO THE SYSTEM IS PROVIDED BY PAPER CARDS WITH MAGNETIC STRIPES
THAT ARE INSERTED INTO THE TURNSTILES.  VENDING MACHINES SELL YOU CARDS FOR
DENOMINATIONS RANGING FROM $.05 TO SEVERAL DOLLARS.
 
I HEARD THAT PEOPLE WERE COUNTERFEITING CARDS IN AN EXTREMELY ELEGANT
LOW TECHNOLOGY FASHION -- THEY WOULD PLACE A CHEAP NICKEL CARD
ON TOP OF AN EXPENSIVE DOLLARS CARD, AND QUICKLY RUN A HOT IRON
OVER THE TOP CARD.  THIS HEATS THE MAGNETIC STRIPE ON THE TOP CARD
PAST THE CURIE POINT -- THE TEMPERATURE AT WHICH IT LOSES ITS MAGNETIC PROPERTI
ES.  ON COOLING BACK DOWN (ALMOST INSTANTLY), IT BECOMES A STORE OF A MAGNETIC
PATTERN AGAIN -- ONE IMPRESSED BY THE CARD ON THE BOTTOM.
A SIMILAR PRINCIPLE IS SOMETIMES USED TO DUPLICATE VIDEOTAPES (SEE THE
BOOK 'INDEPENDENT VIDEO').  HAS ANYBODY OUT THERE EVER TRIED THIS?
IF SO, HAVE I DESCRIBED THE TECHNIQUE RIGHT?  ANY FURTHER TIPS NEEDED?
 
THIS TECHNIQUE MAY BE APPLICABLE TO OTHER CARD SYSTEMS, KEEP IN TOUCH.

Message number 9157 is 13 lines from FRED FIN
To ALL at 04:25:41 on 17-May-81.
Subject: Dual Tone Coin Beeps

The dual tone beeps and the single tone beeps are identical in all
respects (length, count, etc) except for one tone  or two at once.
 
Frequencies, durations, etc are in a TAP back issue, I don't know
which one.
 
Also when practicing (and also when for real), don't have the tones
too loud or too soft.  Have your listener listen to real coins and then
the fake ones, and mark your volume control when they are of an equal
loudness.
 
A quick method I once used to destroy a cassette of beeps was to chuck
it into the microwave oven of the college cafeteria, which was nearby. 

Message number 9163 is 8 lines from SYSOP
To Gary Mason at 14:24:34 on 17-May-81.
Subject: no 450 baud

Hi Gary,
   The 8BBS serial line interface to the modem does not have a very
sophisticated baud rate generator.  It can only handle 110, 150, 300,
600, 1200, 2400, 4800 & 9600 baud.  Obviously the last 3 rates aren't
useable on a dial-up line.  No doubt 450 baud would be just fine, but
we can't run the interface at that speed.  I've had reports from a 
user in Berkeley running a PMMI at 600, so you should be OK from San
Jose.  Regards,..


Message number 9164 is 14 lines from SYSOP
To Paul Traina at 14:36:47 on 17-May-81.
Subject: Auto-bauding

Hi Paul,
   A BASIC 'FOR - NEXT' loop is the main part of the low speed baud rate
recognition code.  The 'FOR - NEXT' loop tries different baud rates and
expects a 'RETURN' char to indicate what speed the user is running at.
   The code looks something like this...
FOR I = 2 to 0         ! Try 300, 150, 110 baud
 SND("Press RETURN")
 D = RCV(0)            ! Get a char from comm line
 IF D = 13 THEN exit   ! Test for RETURN char
NEXT I                 ! Not a RETURN, try next rate
The FOR statement would be changed to FOR I = 3 to 0 to support 600 baud
login.  There is actually more code between the FOR and the NEXT to handle
user time-outs, etc.. so it would require a lot more code to handle out-
of-sequence baud rate testing.  Regards,..

Message number 9175 is 20 lines from SYSOP
To Chuck Hurlbut at 17:08:21 on 17-May-81.
Subject: more on "marked msg's"

Hi Chuck,
   Seems like you missed my msg #8960 where I explained my some of my views
on "marked msg" retrieval.  By nature I'm a generous person, which might be
part of the reason why I dislike "marked msg" retrieval.  To me the "marked
msg" concept indicates stinginess on the part of the software designer in
that the user is required to initiate the request to be able to read a msg
later by typeing a char during a narrow time window.  It smacks of 'batch'
operation in that what the user desires (to read that msg) is not available
until later after some portion of the summary is scanned through. Then the 
sys will dump the "marked msg's" when activated with some other 'special
char', usually the '*'.  The 8BBS selective and/or sequential msg retrieval
methods are 'generous' in that the software wants to give you all the msg's
and will do so immediately unless specifically requested to NOT do so.
Since a selective or sequential msg retrieval combines the functions of the
Q, S and R functions there is really no need to ever use the  S  function.
It is only included for CBBS compatability.
   To summarize... the "marked msg" concept represents the opposite view of
the 8BBS selective/sequential msg retrieval method.  The "marked msg"
implementation will NOT give you a msg unless you request it.  The 8BBS
method WILL give you msg's immediately unless you want to skip them.  Regards

Subject: 212A DATA SET INFO

TECHNICAL SPECIFICATION SUMMARY FOR DATA SET 212A
 
Data Rates:
   Low-Speed Mode:
     0 to 300 Bits Per Second (BPS) Asynchronous Format
   High-Speed Mode:
     1200 BPS +1.0% -2.5% Character-Asynchronous Format
     1200 BPS Synchronous Format
 
Operation:
   Low-Speed Mode:
     Asynchronous,Binary,Serial
   High-Speed Mode:
     Character-Asynchronous Format or Bit-Syschronous Format,Binary,Serial
 
Operating Mode: Full-Duplex at all speeds
 
Line-Requirement: 2-wire switched network
 
         <CONT..>

Received Line Signal Detector Operation:
   Turn ON 155 +/- 50 milliseconds after receiving line signal
   Turn OFF 17+/- 7 milliseconds after loss of line signal
   
Interface Connector And Cable:
   Customer equipment must provide a 25-pin Cinch or Cannon Type
     DB-19604-432 (MALE) connector plug with Cinch Type DB-51226-1 hood
     (or equivlent). Interface cable provided by customer should conform
     to EIA standards.
     
AC Power:
   117 volts +/-10%, 60 Hz +/-5%. Single data set consumes 9 watts max.
   Power outlet should be a conventional three-wire type not under switch
     control.

Message number 9187 is 13 lines from Chuck Hurlbut
To ALL at 23:41:44 on 17-May-81.
Subject: 212a modem the greatest. ven-tel

I just picked up a VEN-TEL md212 Plus modem, and let me tell you it is
an experience. It is a smart modem and once you plug a terminal into it
and hook it to the line, you just set back and watch it run. It dials the
number for you and displays what happened on your terminal. If the line
is BUSY it says so and tries again. If it finally gets through it rings
the terminals bell and prints "ONLINE". It runs 300 baud or 1200 baud
and can remember 5 stored numbers + the last number dialed. To dial
a number you just type K on your terminal and it will ask for the number.
It can recognize a dial tone, busy signal, and a ring. Needless to say I
think it is great. So just check it out before you spend those hard
earned bucks on one that does less. I am not sure what it cost cause
I have not received the bill yet. 
So far the 1200 baud on 8bbs is running great.

Message number 9199 is 17 lines from Phil Reed
To mark thorson at 08:38:04 on 18-May-81.
Subject: phreaking

suprisingly enough, I tend to agree with you. I believe that phreaks *are*
a valuable addition to our sort of society, if for no other reason, then
to find the holes that exist.
       As for breaking into computers, well, the justification needs to
be very carefully defined. While crashing the machine, deleting files, etc
can be concidered serious, under certain circumstances so can the using
of machine resources (time, etc) if these resources are scarce and the
machine usage is important. 
       As for bell, you're right. Presumably bell had a reason to leave
those numbers out without access codes, but it's still dumb. I should poke
around the ess here and see if I can find the bell numbers.
        I still maintain that copying and passing around software is
morally lousy. I have made copies of protected software, (visicalc, etc)
to use as backups. If Personal Software doesn't like that, well they
can just kiss off. However, Mr. Lee's idea of passing around stuff
like candy pisses me off worse than anything.
                                       ...phil

physical laws, can bend or break them anytime He choses in order to

the age of horses and wagons fade into the age of space.  The smallest
piece used to be the cell, which bowed soon to the nucleus, which
gave way to DNA which is giving way to mesons, quarks, and semi
quarks.  We as organisms are swimming in a sea of information we
cannot receive but we know it is there because our instruments can
receive it.  The smaller gets smaller and the large gets larger

Message number 9228 is 20 lines from Shannon Nash
To ALL at 00:11:18 on 19-May-81.
Subject: Information Density

I have been on several BBS's in the last few days and my impression
is the amount of information in any one message or the information
obtained in a unit of time is dreadfully low.  Of course, the name
Bulletin Board implies this from the start.
 
I would be much happier with messages of several hundred to about 
two thousand words, sort of like a magazine article.  
 
I don't think this will happen until several megabytes of storage
(available at both ends)
and high-speed modems and automatic machine access of BBS's is
common, however.
 
Also this depends on your style of communication.  I have essentially
described exchanges of long-winded messages.  Perhaps this is more
closely approached on actual conferencing systems.  I see a lot of
messages are of the form "Where can I find ....", "You can get it here...".
My message just befor this one is like that.
 
Well, that is all for this long-winded communication.     Shannon

Message number 9245 is 12 lines from SYSOP
To All at 16:49:34 on 20-May-81.
Subject: 8BBS phone line prob's

Some of you may have noticed that the 8BBS dial-up number hasn't been
working for the past couple of days.  Seems that if a phone is left
"off-hook" for a while the CO disconnects service to the line.  I've
always had service restored within a few hours of going back "on-hook"
but this time it didn't work.  So... I logged a trouble call with PT&T
and they said that they needed access to the phone to check it out,
'twas very odd since he didn't do anything but look at the modem and
phone and then said that "the problem" was fixed, sure 'nuf was, too.
Almost gave me the feeling that PT&T just wanted an excuse to see what
was on the other end of the line that went to 296-5799.  Anyway, I've
now learned that the 'proper' way to disable service to a phone is to 
NOT leave the receiver "off-hook", but instead just unplug the phone.

Message number 9253 is 6 lines from Mark Thorson
To DEC HACKS at 21:06:13 on 20-May-81.
Subject: FOR WHAT IT'S WORTH

I DON'T KNOW IF THIS INFO WILL EVER BE USEFUL
TO ANY OF YOU, BUT ALL THE DEC ROUND KEYS ARE THE SAME.
THE KEY TO THE FRONT CONSOLE OF YOUR PDP-8 WILL FIT IN
A VAX (FOUND THAT OUT BY FITTING THE KEY FROM A PDP-8 INTO
A VAX).  NATURALLY, THE ANCIENT FLAT KEYS (ALA PDP-5)
AND THE PDP-11 FLAT KEYS (CIRCA 11/10) DON'T.

Message number 9258 is 19 lines from Phil Reed
To joshua gordon at 11:21:06 on 21-May-81.
Subject: the further adventures of ackermann's fu

Well, after doing some digging, I found Ackermann's function written up
in the Jan 1979 Dr. Dobb's. 1 page article. Turns out my original
algorithm was correct after all; the article lists some results and
mine correspond exactly. The article's values die at A(4,2), as does
my Apple. So, I decided to try the BFBI approach. (BFBI=brute force,
bloody ignorance). I quick-hacked up an APL version for the 370/158
that I have access to at work, and let her rip. After running out of
stack space a couple of times, I allocated a stack of 10,000 (equivilent
of around 40Kbytes) and let her rip again. Still ran out of stack, with
430 active calls of ACK waiting to be resolved. I'll push it to the
limit here when I get the chance (not during the day; machine's too
loaded) and I may add a counter to keep track of total number of calls
to ACK. (oh, yeah, when I tried to calculate ACK(4,2), and ran out of
stack at 10,000, the machine showed something like 4 MINUTES of CPU time
burned, in about 6 minutes of real time. Christ! Do you realize how much
that is???)
                                               ...phil
p.s. I saw your name on a ConferenceTree system. I just discovered the
thing. Kind of wierd, huh?

Message number 9269 is 4 lines from George Burdell
To Mark Thorson at 07:48:59 on 22-May-81.
Subject: Totalizers

In order for the phones to work with ACS (the automatic coin
collect system) the totalizers have to be converted to 1700/2200.
The timings are 80Ms on/off for nickels and dimes and 35Ms on/off
for quarters.  Prior to conversion to two tone, it was 2200Hz.

Message number 9276 is 19 lines from Mike VanPelt
To phil reed at 18:41:00 on 22-May-81.
Subject: Religionists/ Right to Life

OK, but remember, you asked for it....
It seems to me that the whole question of abortion, right
or wrong, centers around one, and only one, point.
That is, at what point is a fetus a human being?  It is
quite obvious that after 6 months you are talking about a
human being. My nephew was born in the 24'th week of my
sister's pregnancy.  You wouldn't claim that he was sub-
human for the first 3 months after his birth, would you?  
I do not necessarily agree that human life begins at 
conception, but I think that a reasonable determination would
be the same criterion by which we determine death- the
presence or absence of heartbeat and/or brain wave activity.
This starts in the fetus in the fourth week (week- not month)
of pregnancy.
Any question of economics, is the child wanted, etc. simply
do not apply, unless you think we should exterminate poor 
people and allow people to kill their children if they become
bothersome, which I am sure horrifies you as much as it
does me.

Message number 9297 is 20 lines from Mark Thorson
To SPRINT'ERS at 13:40:06 on 23-May-81.
Subject: TRAPS

I DON'T KNOW IF THIS WOULD HELP, BUT THERE ARE UNPUBLISHED SPRINT
NUMBERS THAT ARE USED FOR DIALING OUT.  DIALING IN TO ONE OF THEM
IS EQUIVALENT TO DIALING IN TO ANY SPRINT NUMBER.  PERHAPS, THEY ARE A SAFE
WAY (OR PARTICULARLY UNSAFE WAY) TO USE THE SYSTEM.
 
THE WAY I RECALL YOU FIND THESE NUMBERS IS TO ASK SPRINT TO DIAL
(415) 111 - 1970.  THIS WORKED (SO I WAS TOLD) FROM AREA CODE 415
A COUPLE YEARS AGO -- WHEN THE A.N.I. WAS 970.  THE SPRINT MACHINES
TRY TO DIAL 111-1970, AND END UP GETTING 970.  THE A.N.I. THEN
SAYS (IN A MECHANICAL VOICE) WHAT YOUR NUMBER IS -- WHICH IS, OF
COURSE, THE NUMBER SPRINT DIALED OUT ON.  DIALING INTO ONE OF THESE NUMBERS
IS LIKE DIALING INTO ANY SPRINT DIALIN.
 
THE BIG QUESTION IS, ARE THESE NUMBERS UNTRAPPED?  OR, ARE CALLS TO THESE
NUMBERS THE MOST SUSPICIOUS CALLS OF ALL?
 
THE A.N.I. CODE IN YOUR AREA IS LIKELY DIFFERENT.  IN 415, IT MAY
HAVE CHANGED. IN 408 (WHERE I LIVE NOW), IT IS 760 -- BUT IT ONLY
WORKS DURING MON-FRI 8AM-5PM.  HAVE FUN
                                VIVA LA REVOLUCION

Message number 9319 is 6 lines from SYSOP
To Kerry Abel at 10:01:47 on 24-May-81.
Subject: Kerry Abel

Hi Kerry,
   The 1200 baud speed recognition is done by the modem.  It can tell if
the originating modem is a 212A type by the tone your modem sends back.
The 8BBS answer modem supplies a 'speed indicator' signal that the 8BBS
program checks to see if 1200 baud is in use and sets the baud rate to
1200.  The A function has no effect for 1200 baud users.  Regards,..

Message number 9339 is 13 lines from Steven Inness
To ERIC MOYER at 04:48:19 on 25-May-81.
Subject: MODEM INFO.

Almost all 0-600 baud formats are bell 103 compatible. The
deaf TTY network uses 45.4545 baud and different frequencies
(1400/1800) vs. 2025/2225 for the 103. The 202 uses
1200/2200Hz. Common baud rates for the 103 are: 50, 75, 110,
134.5, 150, 200, 300, and 600. Digital modems such as the
MC14412 have trouble (I could not get my 14412 to work at 600)
above 300 baud since they can only resolve integer cycles.
Digital modems work by effectively timing the duration
between
zero-crossings and producing a "1" if shorter than a specific
duration. The comparison is 2125Hz for the high group and
1170Hz for the low group. Happy modulating, -SLI
P.S. You all do know MODEM stands for "MOdulator-DEModulator", right?

Message number 9352 is 11 lines from Eric Moyer
To Steven Inness at 10:30:24 on 25-May-81.
Subject: Modems

Thanks for the info about the modems.  (did I ask for it?  I haven't
been on for so long...) Yes, I knew what modem stands for.  About
a null modem, I'm not sure what issue of Byte its in, but its a recent
one.  All a null modem is is a box that enables to terminals to connect
together.  If your terminal or computer doesn't use the handshaking
signals, then all you need to do is cross the rs232 data lines.
ie:  connect data in to data out and vice versa(pin 2 to pin 3
and vice versa) if it does use handshaking, there are a couple other
lines that have to be crossed also, but I don't remember which ones
they are....
                                               Eric

Message number 9378 is 8 lines from George Burdell
To Meg Kazmar at 05:41:51 on 27-May-81.
Subject: Exclusion Key

An exclusion key has the function of making sure that no other
equipment can access the line while the exclusion key is activated.
Two examples:
       1. An exclusion key can disconnect all other extensions
          so that privacy is "ensured."
       2. An exclusion key can make sure that a phone and a
          modem/DAA are never both "off-hook" at the same time
          mainly so that the modem doesn't get disturbed.


Message number 9379 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To All at 05:49:51 on 27-May-81.
Subject: WATS restructuring

Effective Monday, 1 June, the way WATS works will change DRASTICALLY.
Currently, there are two types of WATS:  10-hour and Full Business Day.
With 10-hour, you pay for the first 10 hours (whether you use it or
not) and with FBD, you pay for the first 240.  In each case you pay
an overtime charge for each 1/10th of an hour of overtime.  If you
had a GROUP of lines (say 10 FBDs) you got 2400 hours of usage and
only got billed overtime when you went over that (even if your first
line got 500 hours, if your total wasn't over 2400, no overtime).
What this meant was that large companies were able to make their
long distance calling "Fixed-Cost", i.e., an individual call had
no added cost (unless it made the lines busy, and caused a need for
a whole additional line).  THIS MEANT THAT NIGHTTIME USE OF WATS
WAS "FREE."
 
NOW COMES A DRASTIC CHANGE:  A WATS line now costs $27.50.  You
pay a certain amount per hour of usage (billed in 1/10th hour
increments).  The amount you pay is highest for the first several
hours, and drops off as you use more (but never drops off to as
low as the old 240 overtime was...).  There are three separate
periods, the same as the DDD periods.  Your usage an any period (cont'd)


Message number 9380 is 20 lines from George Burdell
To All at 05:57:58 on 27-May-81.
Subject: WATS Restructuring, cont'd.

counts only toward the reduced rate during that period.  For the
late-night/weekend period, you pay about $0.12/minute for a "Service
Area 5" line if you are on one of the coasts -- but there is no
reduction for large amounts of usage during the night.
 
At least TWO really important things have happened:
       1. Companies which had only SA 5 lines should start placing
          nearby calls as DDD calls -- it's cheaper.  What they
          really need is the appropriate mix of a few lines for
          each area, and a smart switch to sort out the calls by
          area code.
       2. IF YOU MAKE (I mean PAY FOR) AT LEAST TEN HOURS OF LONG
          DISTANCE CALLS A MONTH YOU SHOULD PROBABLY BUY ONE OF
          THESE FOR YOUR HOME!  (yes, you can get one for only
          $27.50... not a lot more than a plain black phone in
          New York or Chicago with metro service).  The things
          to remember are that you can only call to outside your
          state and that calls within a few hundred miles should
          not be made on SA5 lines.
I'll put the whole rate structure in here in a couple of days.

Message number 9483 is 14 lines from SYSOP
To Dave Starr at 13:11:42 on 30-May-81.
Subject: Warning...

Hi Dave,
   Evidently you didn't understand the message.  I'll try to phrase it more
emphatically.  YOU ARE !NOT! TO DELETE MESSAGES THAT DON'T BELONG TO YOU.
8BBS is NOT a phreakers BBS, it is not a religionists BBS, it is not any
one sort of BBS.  This BBS is probably the most 'open' BBS in the country
in terms of message content policy.  You are to refrain from deleting
msg's that are not TO or FROM you.  Even though some msg's may not interest
you, other users may wish to read them.  You should learn how to use the
^C key to skip msg's or learn how to do selective msg retrieval.  I hope
you understand that you are NOT in charge of deciding which msg's are to
be killed.  The hundred or so msg's you 'killed' have been revived to
allow other users access to them.
   About loging in again with a 'new' name without having to re-dial...
That is most definitely NOT going to be implemented.

Message number 9492 is 14 lines from SYSOP
To Mark Thorson at 10:10:42 on 31-May-81.
Subject: BBS fade out

Hi Mark,
   I read Frank's article in Kilobaud about BBS's fading out.  Most of
his comments about the negative aspects of running your own BBS are
very true.  Amount of time and money spent doing daily, weekly, monthly
file maintenance and hardware upkeep, equipment usage and wear, no income,
abuse and threats from users, etc...  I estimate it costs me about $40
per month in electricity for the system and dedicated air-conditioner.
About another $20 per month for supplies like paper and printer ribbons.
I sorta justify the cost by rationalizing, that since I don't smoke, it's
probably about what I'd pay per month if I did smoke.  So I just consider
it as a fixed expense.  No, I have no immediate plans to shut things down,
but I am thinking about a way to raise some money to cover a small amount
of the expenses some time in the future.  Will let you know if anything
comes of it.  Regards,..

was/is? a RDL on this 296-5799 line.  It's function was described as a

someone who calls a number on the 'other side' of the RDL coupler.  Does
any of this sound useful or interesting?  Regards,..

Message number 9558 is 16 lines from SYSOP
To ALL at 00:19:38 on 03-Jun-81.
Subject: 8BBS user stat's

8BBS user statistics based on 826 users data
 
246 (29.7%) upper / lower case users   580 (70.2%) upper case only users
815 (98.6%) full duplex users           11 ( 1.3%) half duplex users
810 (98.0%) users enable line feeds     16 ( 1.9%) disable line feeds
311 (37.6%) harcopy terminal users     515 (62.3%) video terminal users
 98 (11.8%) users with XON prompts     728 (88.1%) with bell promts
 71 ( 8.5%) users have nulls set       768 (92.9%) users with 80 char lines
 
684 (82.8%) novice users               142 (17.1%) expert users
199 (24.0%) users with login passwords
 
This info was based on info stored in the user data file with the
U  function.  I suspect that many users don't have their system
paramaters set to what they want and just use the appropriate
function each time they log in to change paramaters to what they want.

Office informing me that a Mr. Lewis DePayne (alias ROSCOE) had nothing
better to do with his time than waste MY time, so he was therefore 
pressing charges against me for "Telephone Harrassment..."!  Taking it
for the joke it was, I took the morning off work (I needed a hair-cut
anyhow...)and went down to where this hearing was to occur...And right
up there on the 18th floor was Lewis, sitting next to his STARR witness,
none other than the illustriuos pain-in-the-patootie DAVE STARR!!!!

Lewis was so nervous that his hands were shaking; his voice was weak...
I thought for sure that he was going to pee his little pants!!  He, (of
course) brought THE TAPE-RECORDER containing THE TAPE, but he never even
got a chance to play it because the hearing officer couldn't have given
a shit.  And neither did Dave get a chance to display the vast amount
of printouts that he dragged along!!  It's just too bad that nobody
gives a flying frig about what either of them have to say!!!  By the
way, I didn't put this message up here to start another war:  I'm just
returning a favour......                          THUNDER

Message number 9600 is 19 lines from Mike VanPelt
To Phil Reed/ Religionists at 19:05:24 on 04-Jun-81.
Subject: Right to Life

I *finally* managed to get through to this bbs!
You put your finger on an interesting irony of the whole right
to life controversy- pro-abortion people are ususally anti-
capital punishment, and anti-abortion people are usually pro
capital punishment.  This is true for me too, and I have done
a good bit of soul-searching about why this should be.  If
you abort someone because s/he may (or may not) be unwanted, 
in which case s/he may (or may not) commit murder, you are
punishing someone for something that you speculate that s/he
may be more inclined to do than the "average" person.  This is
open to grotesque abuses- ghetto blacks have a statistically 
higher crime rate, so. . . 
On the other hand, in capital punishment, an individual who
has commited murder is being punished for his/her(argh!)
own act.  It is a question of an individual's responsiblity for
his/her own actions.  
   As for the 'unwanted child' question, with a 10-year waiting
list for adoptions,I question whether there are any unwanted
children at all- SOMEONE wants them...

Message number 9603 is 11 lines from SYSOP
To Ted Shapin at 20:20:45 on 04-Jun-81.
Subject: file xfer method?

Hi Ted,
   Thank you very much for taking the time and doing the work
of comparing the two lists.   You didn't say what you were
using to send the file, but it sounded like you can 'trigger'
on a specific char.  If so, you should trigger on XON code,
ASCII 021 (same as ^Q).  You should have 'prompt with no bell'
set (P function).  
   To send the file, you should activate your prog when at the 
1st line prompt (1?) and the prog should wait for a XON before
sending the next line.  That method does work.  Looking forward
to updating the 'O' list.

Message number 9624 is 7 lines from SYSOP

Subject: ^S , S prob'

Hi George,
   'Nuther local 1200 baud user left a comment indicating no problems
with using  ^S  or  S.  Perhaps there is too much transmission delay
if you get a satellite link?   I've had no problems at 600 baud.  There
is a 16 char 'typeahead' buffer, so if you send a ^S within 16 char's
of the end of the line, it will finish sending the line before stopping.
   Clever use of the VT52 hold screen mode...  Regards,..

Message number 9638 is 13 lines from Allan Hessenflow
To Shannon Nash at 09:40:54 on 07-Jun-81.
Subject: 212 freqs

A 212 modem uses dibit phase shift keying.  The originating
end xmits a 1200 hz carrier and receives a 2400 hz carrier.
The answering end xmits 2400 and rcvs 1200 hz carriers.
It sends one dibit (or 2 bits) at a time, here are the phase
shifts for different dibits.
Dibit          Phase shift
 00                 90 degrees
 01                  0
 10                180
 11                270
It is capable of running synchronous or character asynchronous
formats.  Hope this helps,    
                       Allan Hessenflow


Message number 9639 is 20 lines from Marc Mosko
To Anyone at 11:25:26 on 07-Jun-81.
Subject: CSI Info...

     Well, I've been a CompuServe (MicroNET) user for a long time now,
and the system has really improved.  Although DISPLA isn't the easiest program
in the world to get along with (and very repetative), it does get the job done.
     There is an option someplace in DISPLA to make it so you're DIRECTLY
logged onto MicroNET, not DISPLA...There is another option (same place as
this one where ever that is) to be put directly into EMIAL if you have new
mail waiting.
     If you're a programmer, you'll love MicroNET....They have just about
every language that you can think of...Here is most of there:
FORTRAN IV and EXTENDED, COBOL, APL, BASIC & extended, SAIL, MACRO, ALGOL,
TECO, ROOT, and many other languages...You have a VERY large amount of core
(private and some public) accessible to you...I don't think that you can
get much public core anymore, but before they would allow your job to
call up alot of it before (now there are just too many users).
     If you're a game player with a big bank account, they have
quit a few good games, and two exellent adventures..The first is the Original
Adventure writen by John Wood at Stanford (don't think it's the same John Wood
as we have on this system...), and the next is an extended version of the
original that is VERY DIFFICULT if you haven't mastered the first!
     They have word processors..........continued next message..

that get the job done fast and without alot of pain...Such as FILGE
(FIle GEnerator) that just alows you to enter text kind of like the 8BBS

binary dumps..don't remember the name.
     All there manuals are writen by them or DEC (they mail the original
manual with supplements), and are reasonably priced.

just that, a CB simulator with 30 indevidual chanals, and private talk modes.
SPCWAR is a startrek type game (you go arround and blast the other people who
are trying to kill you), and is based on a point scoring system not a death
rate!

Message number 9641 is 20 lines from Marc Mosko
To All at 11:43:10 on 07-Jun-81.
Subject: MicroNET PPNs

     The MicroNET PPN is a very basic thing (its alos in the standard
format for all PDP-10s useing a TOPs-10 monitor [there's is just modified]).
First PPN= Project, Programmer Number
In this examle I will use that good old PPN 70000,1.
Project =70000   Programmer #= 1
The project # determins what kind of account it will be, and the programmer #
is just to keep track of all the PPNs in that project.  ALL PPNs ARE OCTAL!
Now, ANY PPN that has a project # of 70000, 70003, 70005 or that ends in
a 1, 3, 5 is a FREE account (no one pays for it)!  These are isued to people
that do something for CSI.
Now, MNET uses the Project number to determin what STATE you're calling from.
If i were to give an entire list it would take alot of space (there are multipa
l project numbers for some and most states).  But, such thigs as 70110
is in CA, 70150 is in MI, 70210 is in NY, etc.
Every so often you might see something like a 313,302 on CB or something..
Well, that is a transfer account from the CompuServe computers (a person
with an account on COMPUSERVE not MNET) useing CB or something...You'll notice
that his Account ID is something like: 0003020010..(think I left out a
0 or two but..) that means that his PPN is 302,10 (or 302,0010..0's before the
first digit in the Programmer # don't are insugnificant)..continued


Message number 9642 is 13 lines from Marc Mosko
To All at 11:47:50 on 07-Jun-81.
Subject: MNET PPNs

     Now, some projects are privlaged.  The 70000 project is privlaged..They
can log on anytime, and execute some programs that normal PPNs can't, etc.
There is also the PPN 1,2.  This is the operator PPN, and can do vertually ANYT
HING!   Of course you'll never see this PPN anywhere, but it's there.  There ar
e the system libraries (1,40- 1,46) the hold the MNET & CSI programs.  There
is the CSI FEEDBK account (12,12 I think), and many others (such as the Tandy
store accounts (the 70005 prject) that are used by the stores).

                Marc Mosko  70110,145

Message number 9695 is 18 lines from Mark Thorson
To ARPANET NOVICES at 17:17:38 on 10-Jun-81.
Subject: RITES OF PASSAGE

I HAVE READ ENOUGH MESSAGES, BOTH PUBLIC AND PRIVATE (SOME ADDRESSED
TO ME, SOME NOT), ASKING HOW TO USE A TIP.  HERE GOES:
 
1.  HIT AN UPPERCASE 'E' WHEN YOU FIRST CONNECT TO THE DIALUP.
2.  AFTER THE TIP BANNER PRINTS, SAY '@ O 123' TO CONNECT TO NODE 123
    (OR SUBSTITUTE YOUR OWN NODE ADDRESS).
3.  SAY '@ C' TO BREAK THE CONNECTION (TO RECONNECT TO ANOTHER NODE).
 
THERE IS MORE STUFF TO IT THAN THIS, OF COURSE, BUT THIS WILL
GET YOU STARTED.  BECAUSE TIP COMMANDS BEGIN WITH '@', YOU MUST SAY
'@@' TO SEND AN '@' TO THE REMOTE HOST.
 
A LITTLE KNOWN FACT -- IF YOU SAY '@ 4 C', YOU WILL BREAK THE
CONNECTION OF THE PARTY ON LINE 4 OF YOUR TIP (WE CALL THAT SOCKET #4).
IN FACT, YOU CAN FORCE ANY COMMANDS ONTO ANY SOCKET ON YOUR TIP.
THIS WAS INTENDED TO ALLOW THINGS LIKE CONTROLLING AN OUTPUT-ONLY
DEVICE CONNECTED TO THE TIP (A LINE PRINTER, FOR EXAMPLE).  
I WONDER WHAT HAVOC WILL BE CAUSED BY TELLING ALL YOU MONSTERS ABOUT THIS.

Message number 9700 is 11 lines from Phil Reed
To arpa novices (and some others) at 06:09:41 on 11-Jun-81.
Subject: more tip stuff

One other thing for all you TIP users: When you first dial up, the TIP
will throw in 2-3 nulls after a CR. You can instruct the TIP to get
rid of these by entering   @D C A   or, if you need more nulls (using
a slow hardcopy terminal?) you enter    @D C E
 
Another thing, the TIP doesn't care if the commands you send it are
in upper or lower case. Also, when you want to send a @ to the host
you're using, you type @ twice, and it will appear on your terminal
*three* times, the first two echoed from the TIP, and the third from
the host.
                                               ...phil

Message number 9726 is 14 lines from Steven Inness
To SYSOP at 02:13:08 on 13-Jun-81.
Subject: Useless subject line.

What character do you use for line cancel? Is there one? If
not, I suggest the standard control-X to cancel input lines.
It would be nice if it was easier to abort from the early
stages of entering a message (Subject?, Protect?, Review).
Control-K should work at this stage. If "E" is accidentally
pressed you are stuck.
 
I have found another bug! There is no control-Q printed
immediately after the ">" prompt when messages are left for
the Sysop at logoff. This locks my keyboard out when I try to
leave comments. The control-Q should be printed by the input
routine, rather than along with the prompt string as you
probably have it.
-Dr. SLI, T.I.D.


Message number 9728 is 14 lines from Steven Inness
To MARCOS WOEHRMANN at 02:15:12 on 13-Jun-81.
Subject: THANKS MSG 9388 & 9397

A while ago I needed to know what the pin 37 frequency was
because I was trying to figure out how their disk interface
works. I asked a friend Apple owner, who said it was 2MHz. I
phoned Apple to ask about how the interface worked. The
engineer I spoke with claimed what I wanted was "proprietary,
confidential, and patented". He mentioned that there is NO
2MHz clock on the Apple bus, and after all, he should know. I
phoned my friend again and he said it was definitly 2MHz. I
was irked by this, so I phoned Apple back and tried to talk
with someone else. I was redirected to the engineer whom I
spoke with earlier. This time he said ABSOLUTELY, POSITIVELY,
UNQUESTIONABLY, STAKE-HIS-MOTHER'S-LIFE-ON-IT, THERE IS NO
2MHz ON THE APPLE BUS. THE FREQUENCY ON PIN 37 IS 1.023MHz
EXACTLY! Two against one now... -SLI


Message number 9729 is 9 lines from Steven Inness
To ERIC MOYER at 02:15:59 on 13-Jun-81.
Subject: MODEM REPLY

You did ask for half of it, the rest was donated.
REM: 'tis better to transmit than to receive.
I saw it, I just can't find the Null Modem article now. I
wanted to see if he wired 4-5, 6-20, or 4-6-8, 5-20, or
whatever. It is everyman for himself (everyperson for itself)
regarding these pins. The RS232 standard is a good simple
standard, but is wholy inappropriate for today's needs. It was
ONLY meant for wiring a dumb terminal to a modem. The only pin
everyone aggrees on is pin 7. -Dr. SLI, T.I.D.

Message number 9734 is 11 lines from SYSOP

Subject: Xpert?

Hi Steven,
   Sounds like you are operating in 'expert' mode...  Welcome msg clearly
states that a ^U cancels the current line input.  Novice mode clearly
states that a  -  is used to back out of msg entry (same as CBBS).  BTW:
^U is standard line input abort (in DEC OS's) not ^X.
   Can't imagine why lack of XON should lock your keyboard.  I'll check the
code and see if it is fixable without too much effort.  I no longer have
much time or interest in doing 8BBS prog mods.  I'm working on a 16 ch,
12 A/D module and a TI Speak & Spell interface.

get a VADIC triple.  Regards,..

Message number 9762 is 7 lines from SYSOP
To Bob Zimmerman at 00:19:49 on 16-Jun-81.
Subject: 600 still OK

Hi Bob,
   Your comment sounded like you thought 8BBS used to run with a PMMI.  Not
so... it was a flakey Novation 4103B that was sometimes useable at 600.
600 baud was (and still is) optional at the callers own choice using the
'A' function to switch to 600 from some lower speed.  The 212A that is
currently in use runs MUCH better at 600.  Give it a try, had reports that
it worked OK at 600 to Berkeley, so it may be OK for you also.  Regards,..

Message number 9779 is 17 lines from John Wood
To dave flory at 01:22:39 on 17-Jun-81.
Subject: use TELEMAIL/IBS INSTEAD!!

If you are considering compuserve, and you are, and you
seem to already have determined that the information utility
features are  more a novelty once you get over the intrique factor
(a 60 cent paper in the morning is a lot cheaper than reading
a paper at 300 baud for $5 an hour) and since you have your own
micro so micro-net timesharing is not really needed, why don't
you check into our TELEMAIL / IBS system which may be exactly
what you are looking for.  It is a global electronic message
system like this board and CBBS Sunnyvale except it reaches much
farther, is accesible via local phone call in most cities, and
features sophisticated person-to-person mail beyond the read-protected
message facitilities common on some boards (and very good here.)
Of course, a major point is that it is multi-user running on
a $500,000 TANDEM NONSTOP(TM) multi-processor main-frame computer
system. So no busy signals and reasonable response time.
If you are interested, check other messages here or on CBBS sunnyvale,
408-737-7543 or leave a msg for MIKE DOVE our system administrator.

Message number 9814 is 4 lines from Mike VanPelt
To dDave Flory at 23:51:58 on 18-Jun-81.
Subject: 2kbbs

To get into 2kbbs, you have to enter 2 cr's, and 1 lf.
  ctl(m), ctl(m), ctl(j).  Then type hello-b200,,4 if you
have a CRT terminal or hello-b200,,3 for paper teminals.
The last number determines what kind of back-spacing to do.


Message number 9817 is 20 lines from John Wood
To phil reed at 01:32:19 on 19-Jun-81.
Subject: telemail/ibs

TELEMAIL/IBS is on TELENET.  Thus there are no hidden
charges for using the telenet network and it is accessible
from every telenet dial-up.  The system feature a very
good electronic message system, multiple bulletin boards
arranged by subject for easy scaning, and multi-user
capability running on a $300,000 TANDEM nonstop computer
syste for high reliability.
TELEMAIL/IBS is the lowest-priced, non-prime time message
system and is also reasonable (but expensive) in prime
time.  We decided to pick the functons everyone wants,
electronic mail (person-to-person private messages) and
bulletin board or public broadcast messages) and offer
the best syste for that.  We don't offer the electrnic
new york times or stuff like that; nor do we want to.
Did you ever notice that a lot of those 'information
utility' stuff which sounds real neat is often an EXTRA
SURCHARGE for use?  Have you checked the prices on
the stock quotations and other EXTRA services they offer
which their advertising does not clearly state COSTS MORE
above their minimum hourly rates?


Message number 9818 is 19 lines from John Wood
To all at 01:36:56 on 19-Jun-81.
Subject: file xfer -telemail/ibs

TELEMAIL/ibs supports file transfers in the following
way:  a 'message' on the system is simply any entity
that a user keys into the system.  If that message
should contain the ascii text of a program or even the
hexadecimal version, that does not matter.
Since TELEMAIL supports the DC1/DC3  (x-on, x-off) flow
control protocol, it is very easy to upload a 'file'
into a message and then have someone else 'download' the
file into their own system.
What makes this easy is the fact that each user is
communicating thru a local phone line, hence much better
transmission and that a message is unlimited in length!
no 16 or 20 line limits.
Also, any message can be saved in an individuals own
private file storage which is currently billed at the
rate of 1 penny per thousand characters per day.
the simple command 'file in archive' will take the current
message and store it away in a file called 'archive'
for example.

Message number 9837 is 20 lines from John Wood
To phil reed at 10:10:24 on 20-Jun-81.
Subject: more telemail info

TELEMAIL/IBS is a turn-key mail system.  There is not
a way to exit out and use the Tandem.  The advantage of
the Tandem as its hardware is the fact that it is the
most reliable system so the TELEMAIL system is up almost
all the time.  Also, a big advantage is that the Tandem
hardware is very modlar.  They can go from a 2 or 3 processor
system up to a 16 processor system with no software changes
(They do not even have to re-compile their programs, if
they did it right.)
So, as the system grows, they can quickly keep up the
load, unlike the other sysems which must rubber-band
together many dec-20/dec-10 computers to expand capacity
or several prime systems.
TELEMAIL/IBS costs only $3.50 per hour during non-prime
time.  Non-prime time is currently 6 pm to 7am mon - Fri and
all day Sat Sun, and certain Holidays.
Effective July 1,1981 (unfortunately) TELEMAIL rates are
doubling.  However, TELEMAIL/IBS will still offer the
$3.50 per hour rate, except non-prime time will be from
9 pm to 7am.  Other rates: $16/hr 7am to 6pm, $8/hr 6 to 9pm

Message number 9901 is 20 lines from John Wood
To all 202 users?? at 20:46:53 on 24-Jun-81.
Subject: about the bell 202

The BELL 202 was the first 1200 baud modem for use over 2 wire
telco lines.  It is half-duplex, that means only one end of
the line can send at a time, and the other end must wait.
The sending line then 'turns the line around' and each end
reverses their role.  The 'reverse interrupt' pin on the RS-232
is a primitive way for the receiver to tell the sender to shut up
and let it get the line immmediately because it has something important
to send (usually a protocol message saying retransmit last msg, etc.)
HALF-DUPLEX MODEMS (which are different from HALF-DUPLEX terminals)
are really only useful for commputer to computer lines, where typically
a file transfer or several thousand characters go down the line in
one direction.  An interactive terminal (or virtual terminal)
such as a CBBS, where the user may type 1 or 2
characters, then wait for the other end to reply, would be
very SLOW with a 202 because there is a minimum hardware delay
required to 'turn the line around.'  Also, note that most
current SATTELITE based communications lines suffer almost a
5 sec 'end to end' line turn-around delay, so satellites ARE NOT
the answer to INTERACTIVE long distance computing (commuting.)
At least, currently.


Message number 9902 is 8 lines from John Wood
To all 202 users at 20:48:43 on 24-Jun-81.
Subject: more about 202 quirks

I think that if you can get 202's cheap (which they seem to 
be available) an interesting use would be a link using two
dedicated phone lines. Then one line could send and the other
could receive.  This would eliminate the line turn-around delays.
Unfortunately, again, i think this would only work from computer-
to computer because each end needs TWO RS-232 ports and the
software (intelligence) to multiplex them (look at one for
incoming data, send data out on the other.)

Message number 9920 is 20 lines from christine davidson
To ALL at 20:43:00 on 25-Jun-81.
Subject: hee

    8BBS is generally implemented as a superset of the CBBS program running
on Ward & Randy's system in Chicago.  As nearly as we can tell, 8BBS does
everything that CBBS does except for reporting the number of characters sent
by the system and the caller.  There are many subtle enhancements in 8BBS
that may not be apparent to someone used to CBBS.  Some of these are...
 . 8BBS Has several features connected with your name that are automatically
        set whenever you dial in. These include such things as terminal
        characteristics (nulls, echo, line-feed) and whether you are a
        novice or expert user (The "U" function is used to set these)
 . 8BBS Allows you to define a password that must be used for you to log in.
 . 8BBS Tells you when you have a message waiting. It also tells you the
        range of the new messages since your last time on the system.
 . 8BBS Allows you to sequentially retrieve messages (that is, you can
        automatically read all the messages from any starting point
        by the use of the "^" or "-" characters during retrieve.)
 . 8BBS Allows messages to be 'private' i.e. they can be read (or
        summarized) only by the sender or receiver).
 . 8BBS Allows you to see previous users ("Z" function)
 . 8BBS Allows you to yell for and talk to the operator ("Y" function)
 . 8BBS Allows you to set your terminal width ("F" function)

Message number 9974 is 11 lines from John Wood
To source/micronet/users at 02:01:35 on 28-Jun-81.
Subject: 1200 'free' on TELEMAIL/IBS

As some of you who own 1200 baud modems are now finding out,
SOURCE, COMPUSERVE, and DOW JONES CHARGE YOU EXTRA IF YOU use
a high speed modem.  DOW JONES (and i assume the others) claims
that if you use the system '4 times faster' charging you 1.5 times
more is still 'a good deal'.
Well, TELEMAIL/IBS does not surcharge for 1200 baud!!! Actually,
TELENET prices all their service based on the assumption you are
using 1200 baud. So, if you use 300 baud, you are actually not
taking full advantage.  BUT NO 1200 BAUD RIP-OFF!!
Just think how much MORE you can do on TELEMAIL/IBS at 1200 baud
and only $3.50 per hour, non-prime time!!!!
